1 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Andrews


NO. 98-0216


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


10 S.W.3d 663; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 134; 43 Tex. Sup. J. 220


October 12, 1999, Argued  
December 23, 1999, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE SEVENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment reversed and trial court's judgment for Wilson reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties petitioned for review from the Court of Appeals for the Seventh District of Texas, which ruled that Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code §143.057(d) governed petitioner's civil services but unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority to a private entity and unconstitutionally infringed upon petitioner city's home rule powers.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was suspended and elected to have his appeal heard by a neutral hearing examiner pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code §143.057(d). Petitioner city sought a declaration that it was under no obligation to comply with §143.057(d). Petitioner argued that Lubbock, Tex, Firemen's and Policemen's Civil Service Ordinance 862 governed its civil services. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of respondents Attorney General and police officer. The appellate court reversed, holding that § 143.057(d) unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority to a private entity and unconstitutionally infringed upon petitioner's home rule power. Petitioner was governed by Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code §§ 143.001-.143 as amended, and respondent officer was therefore entitled to have his disciplinary appeal decided before private hearing examiners. Failing to demonstrate that § 143.057(d) would always operate unconstitutionally, petitioner's facial challenge failed. Judgment of appellate court was reversed, and trial court's ruling was reinstated.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and trial court's judgment reinstated. Petitioner was governed by amendments to the Civil Service Act and respondent had the right to have appeal heard by a neutral hearing examiner. Petitioner's constitutional challenges failed, as petitioner could not show that the statute would always operate unconstitutionally.

 

2 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fleming Foods of Tex. v. Rylander


NO. 97-1044


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


6 S.W.3d 278; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 127


November 18, 1998, Argued  
December 9, 1999, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 10, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Tex. LEXIS 57.

ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of court of appeals reversed and case remanded to trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment by the Court of Appeals for the Third District of Texas in favor of respondent in petitioner's suit to recover tax refunds as an indirect taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, who paid sales taxes to vendors, was audited by respondent, state comptroller, for sales and use tax deficiencies. Petitioner obtained assignment of refund rights from some vendors, but the assignments were not executed until more than four years after petitioner had paid the tax. Respondent assessed a deficiency against petitioner for the taxes. Petitioner requested a redetermination hearing and filed for refunds. Respondent agreed petitioner was entitled to some refunds but denied others claiming they were barred by the four-year statute of limitations. The trial court and the appellate court found in favor of respondent. Petitioner sought review alleging it had a right to file for refunds as an indirect taxpayer. Reversing and remanding, the court held the Texas Tax Code's language permitted an indirect taxpayer to seek refunds of sales taxes. Petitioner's requests were timely filed, thus the four-year statute of limitations did not apply.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded; petitioner as an indirect taxpayer was permitted to seek refunds of sales taxes where the refund request was timely filed.

 

3 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brainard v. State


NO. 98-0578


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


12 S.W.3d 6; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 112; 43 Tex. Sup. J. 12


February 10, 1999, Argued  
October 7, 1999, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE SEVENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and reinstated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs petitioned for review of Court of Appeals of the Seventh District of Texas' decision remanding case for jury trial, and holding plaintiffs barred from recovering fees, in a case to determine whether conditions affected by closing the Sanford Dam should be considered by surveyors in marking gradient boundary.


OVERVIEW: The differences between the parties' surveys in the boundary dispute were based on conflicting legal theories, and did not present a factual dispute, thus the court could resolve the matter and remand to the trial court was not necessary. The court held that changes brought about or influenced by the dam must be considered in marking the gradient boundary of a river, so long as the riparian owner did not cause or contribute to the artificial influence. They therefore concluded that a survey of the disputed area must account for present, i.e., post-dam, conditions on the Canadian River by gradient boundary methodology. They held that trial court did not err in rendering judgment declaring that plaintiffs' survey marked the gradient boundary of the Canadian River in the disputed area. They agreed with the court of appeals, that the legislative resolution bared the plaintiffs from recovering their attorney's and surveyor's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirm that attorney's and surveyor's fees were not recoverable; reversed the remand to the trial court; and reinstated the trial court's judgment declaring that the plaintiffs' survey correctly marked the boundary between the State's riverbed and the riparian tracts.

 

4 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Quick v. City of Austin


NO. 96-1154


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


7 S.W.3d 109; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 110; 42 Tex. Sup. J. 1217


November 3, 1997, Argued  
September 30, 1999, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Amended Opinion of May 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tex. LEXIS 82.



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment reversed in part, and judgment modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On application for writ of error to the Court of Appeals for the Third District of Texas, petitioners appealed the court's modification of a trial court order pertaining to permit applications for property development.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed original permit applications for property development; due to ongoing development from these permit applications, petitioners applied for subsequent site development permits after enactment of a local ordinance. The court reversed the appellate court, concluding Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 481.143 gave petitioners the right to have appellee consider permit application solely on basis of any orders, regulations, ordinances, or other duly adopted requirements in effect at time original application for was filed, and general savings clause applied to the repeal of § 481.143. Under the previous version of § 481.143, any subsequent permit applications filed or approved between September 1, 1987 and September 1, 1997 were governed by only the rules, regulations, and ordinances in effect in 1985 when the original applications for preliminary subdivision approval were filed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Court of appeals erred in holding that only the subsequent permit applications from original permit applications filed after September 1, 1987 were governed by the ordinances in effect at the time of the original application.

 

5 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Bd. of the Tex. DOT v. El Paso Indep. Auto. Dealers Ass'n, Inc.


No. 98-0514


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


1 S.W.3d 108; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 99; 42 Tex. Sup. J. 1128



August 26, 1999, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE EIGHTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court rendered judgment in an action by respondents, an association of used car dealers, declaring that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 728.001 through 728.004 were unconstitutional and enjoined enforcement of those provisions by state authorities. After having its appeal dismissed, petitioner, the state's motor vehicle board, filed a petition for review of the decision of the Court of Appeals for the Eighth District of Texas.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, an association of used car dealers, sued various local officials of the El Paso area to enjoin them from enforcing Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 728.001-728.004, the Blue Law, and to have it declared unconstitutional because it prohibited the sale of cars on consecutive weekend days. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of respondents. The appellate court held that petitioner, the state's motor vehicle board, and the state's attorney general had the right to appeal under the doctrine of virtual representation, but concluded that the attorney general had waived that right by way of a letter in which it stated that it believed the local officials would litigate the matter; the local officials later voluntarily dismissed their appeal. Petitioner's appeal was dismissed. On review, the court noted that the waiver issue rested squarely on the substance of the attorney general's letter. As such, the court held that nothing about the attorney general's letter indicated an intention to "expressly renounce" or otherwise waive any right the attorney general or petitioner had to have the case fully defended or appealed. Thus, the court reversed and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of petitioner's appeal of judgment declaring sections of Texas's transportation code unconstitutional and enjoining enforcement of those sections was reversed and remanded. Petitioner did not waive its right to appeal because a letter by the state's attorney general stating the belief that local officials would litigate the matter did not expressly renounce any right petitioner had to have the case fully litigated.

 

6 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Owens Corning v. Carter


No. 97-1162, No. 97-1163, No. 97-1164, No. 97-1165, No. 97-1166


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


997 S.W.2d 560; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 72; 42 Tex. Sup. J. 883


September 9, 1998, Argued  
July 1, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7551.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 250TH DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed trial court's judgment that section 71.051 does not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause. Because sections 71.031(a)(3), 71.052(b), and 71.052(c) are constitutional with respect to the challenges asserted by Plaintiffs, reversed the trial court's judgment to the contrary, and instructed the court to vacate its orders enjoining Defendants from attempting to enforce those provisions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporations challenged the order of the 250th District Court of Travis County, (Texas), declaring that several state statutes were unconstitutional and enjoining defendants from attempting to enforce the subject statutes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured individuals brought five separate lawsuits in the state against defendants, various corporations, for personal injuries resulting from asbestos exposure. In the instant consolidated direct appeals, the court considered the constitutionality of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. §§ 71.031(a)(3), 71.051, and 71.052(b) and (c). The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's judgment that § 71.051 did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, because it did not discriminate between citizens and noncitizens of the forum state. The court reversed the lower court's judgment regarding §§ 71.031(a)(3), 71.052(b), and 71.052(c), and held that they were constitutional with respect to the challenges asserted by plaintiffs. The court found that §71.031(a)(3) was not unconstitutionally retroactive and did not violate U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, Tex. Const. art. 1, § 16, or the open courts clause. The court went on to find that § 71.052(b) and (c) did not violate Tex. Const. art. III, § 56, the Privileges and Immunities Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, or the equal protection provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Tex. Const. art. I, §3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that one of the statutes was constitutional in that it did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause. The court reversed the order of the trial court declaring the remaining state statutes unconstitutional and held that these statutes did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause, the open courts clause, equal protection provisions, or any other state or federal statute.

In re Nolo Press/Folk Law


No. 98-0724


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


991 S.W.2d 768; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 35


October 21, 1998, Argued  
April 15, 1999, Delivered



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Nolo Press's petition for mandamus is dismissed for want of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator publisher filed a petition for writ of mandamus compelling respondent, unauthorized practice of law committee, to produce documents and information related to respondent's operations in general, and in particular to its current investigation into whether relator's publications constituted the unauthorized practice of law in Texas.


OVERVIEW: Respondent unauthorized practice of law committee wrote relator publisher a letter, requesting it to provide information about activities it had engaged in, which might have constituted the unauthorized practice of law. Relator responded, but was later contacted for attendance at a hearing. Relator requested information from respondent regarding the complaint, the investigation, the hearing process, and respondent's activities and authority, but respondent refused to provide it. Prior to the hearing, relator petitioned for a writ of mandamus compelling respondent to produce the names of its subcommittee members; the dates, times, locations, agenda, and minutes of past and future meetings; copies of respondent's internal rules and procedures; and all internal documents related to respondent's investigation of relator. In addition, relator requested that the 1986 order be clarified, modified, or construed. The court found that it did not have jurisdiction under Tex. Const. art. V, § 3, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 22.002(a), or Tex. Const. art. II, § 1 to issue mandamus against respondent and vacated its 1986 order because the records were confidential under Tex. R. Jud. Admin. 12.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed relator's petition for mandamus for want of jurisdiction and vacated its order concerning the confidentiality of records of respondent.

 

8 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bradley v. State ex rel. White


No. 97-1135


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


990 S.W.2d 245; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 33; 42 Tex. Sup. J. 513


September 28, 1998, Argued  
April 8, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at City of Roanoke v. Town of Westlake, 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 4414 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, May 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE SECOND DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
State ex rel. White v. Bradley, 956 S.W.2d 725, 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5761 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment reversed and judgment rendered for Bradley on State's quo warranto action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Court of Appeals for the Second District of Texas decision that reversed the judgment that granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, in a quo warranto action by plaintiff that sought a declaration that defendant was not the mayor and that another person was.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought judicial enforcement, through a quo warranto action, of its decision to remove defendant from the seat as mayor. The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals that reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant. Pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002, the proceedings for the removal of defendant as mayor were governed by the state civil procedures and evidence court rules. The aldermen of the city were the judges in this removal proceeding, and violated Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 605 by sitting as judges in the proceeding where they also acted as witnesses. As with Fed. R. Evid. 605, under the Texas rule, a judge could not also act as a witness. As two aldermen-judges also testified as witnesses, they violated defendant's due process rights during the removal proceedings. Due to the defective proceedings, the court entered judgment in favor of defendant, finding that he was still the lawful mayor. Due to the conclusion that defendant negated an element of the plaintiff's quo warranto action, that the aldermen lawfully removed defendant, the court did not need to reach the remaining grounds supporting defendant's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals that reversed the grant of defendant's motion for summary judgment was reversed, and judgment was granted in favor of defendant, because defendant negated an element of the plaintiff's quo warranto case by showing that he was not lawfully removed from the seat as mayor. The court did not need to reach the remaining arguments made to support the grant of defendant's motion for summary judgment.

 

9 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re Barr


Inquiry No. 67


REVIEW TRIBUNAL OF TEXAS


13 S.W.3d 525; 1999 Tex. LEXIS 15



March 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at: 13 S.W.3d 525 at 562.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of February 13, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tex. LEXIS 34.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's Motion for Rehearing overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent judge moved for rehearing of the Review Tribunal's findings in a disciplinary proceeding brought under the Texas Rules for the Removal or Retirement of Judges on the subject of respondent's judicial conduct.


OVERVIEW: The special master found respondent judge had violated various canons of the Texas Constitution and the Texas Code of Judicial Conduct. The review tribunal entered findings, and respondent moved for rehearing of the findings. The court granted respondent's motion. Tex. Const. art. V, § 1-a(6)A, and the Texas Code of Judicial Conduct Canons 2A, 3B(3), 3B(4), 3B(6), and 3B(8) were not unconstitutionally vague. The Code of Judicial Conduct furnished sufficient specification of the judicial conduct that warranted disciplinary action. The forgiveness doctrine was not applicable, and the state judicial conduct commission (commission) was not required to publish its annual report. Respondent's due process rights were not violated when he was denied the opportunity to make an oral argument before the commission on the constitutional issues allegedly involved in the case.


OUTCOME: The court overruled respondent's motion for rehearing because the Texas Code of Judicial Conduct and the Texas Constitution were not unconstitutionally vague concerning judicial conduct that warranted disciplinary action and because respondent's due process rights were not violated when he was denied the opportunity to make an oral argument before the state judicial conduct commission.

In re Bay Area Citizens Against Lawsuit Abuse


No. 97-0812


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


982 S.W.2d 371; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 157; 42 Tex. Sup. J. 182


February 3, 1998, Argued  
December 10, 1998, Delivered



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Mandamus relief conditionally granted with respect to those portions of discovery orders requiring BACALA to disclose its contributors' identities.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner community group against lawsuit abuse filed for a writ of mandamus complaining of two discovery orders of the trial court (Texas), which required petitioner to produce certain documents and answer certain deposition questions concerning the identities of its contributors. Petitioner further complained that the trial court improperly denied its plea to the jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court ordered petitioner community group against lawsuit abuse to disclose its contributors' names and denied petitioner's plea that respondent taxpayers did not have standing to bring suit, petitioner filed for writ of mandamus. On review, the court held that petitioner was not entitled to mandamus relief for the denial of its jurisdictional plea because petitioner failed to show that it lacked an adequate remedy by appeal. In conditionally granting mandamus relief with respect to the disclosure orders, the court held that the orders violated petitioner's right to freedom of association under U.S. amend. I. The court held that petitioner made a prima facie showing that the orders burdened its rights under U.S. amend. I. Specifically, petitioner submitted evidence that its supporters had been subject to boycott threats, and that individuals opposed to petitioner's agenda had boycotted the business establishments of persons affiliated with petitioner. The court further held that respondents failed to show a substantial relation between the identity of petitioner's contributors, corporate or individual, and respondent's goal in demanding disclosure thereof.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted mandamus relief with respect to portions of the trial court's discovery orders requiring petitioner community group against lawsuit abuse to disclose its contributors' identities because such orders violated petitioner's First Amendment freedom of association rights. The court found that petitioner failed to show that it lacked an adequate remedy by appeal from the trial court's denial of its jurisdiction plea.

 

11 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Commission for Lawyer Discipline v. Benton


No. 97-0228


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


980 S.W.2d 425; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 121; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 1250


February 5, 1998, Argued  
July 14, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing of Cause Overruled December 31, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner discipline commission requested review of a decision by the Texas Court of Appeals reversing an order of discipline imposed by the trial court on respondent attorney. The court of appeals reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the case on the sole ground that Tex. R. Disciplinary P. 3.06(d) was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorney had been disciplined for writing an abusive post-judgment letter to jurors who rendered a verdict against respondent's client. Respondent admitted that he wrote the letter to influence the jurors' future conduct. Respondent claimed the disciplinary rule that he violated was unconstitutional under the Federal and Texas Constitutions. The appellate court agreed and found that Tex. R. Disciplinary P. 3.06(d) was void for vagueness and dismissed the action. Respondent appealed, and the supreme court reversed because respondent's letter threatened to damage the jury system, and the rule's prohibition on comments calculated to influence future jury service did not violate the U.S. Const. amend I. The court also decided that the rule was not overbroad and did not violate equal protection. The court did agree that the term "embarrass" contained in the rule was unconstitutionally vague, and the court narrowed the construction of the term "harass" in the rule. The court, noting that the trial court did not specify which provision of rule 3.06(d) respondent violated, remanded the action for trial court to determine how its decision might affect respondent's punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded for a new punishment hearing. The court concluded that the provision of the lawyer discipline rules prohibiting respondent attorney's attempt to influence jurors' future jury service was constitutional and remanded so that the trial court could confine respondent's punishment to a violation of the correct provision and render punishment accordingly.

 

12 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Perry v. S.N.


No. 97-0573


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


973 S.W.2d 301; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 118; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 1162


January 7, 1998, Argued  
July 3, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.

This Opinion Substituted on Overrule of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of May 8, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. LEXIS 77.
Perry v. S.N., 1998 Tex. LEXIS 77 (Tex., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant day care center operators sought rehearing of their petition for a writ of error from the Court of Appeals for the Third District of Texas, which had reversed a trial court's summary judgment for defendants and held that a violation of the Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 261.101(a), 261.109 child abuse reporting requirement was negligence per se in a suit brought by plaintiff parents individually and on behalf of their children.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parents filed suit individually and as friends of their children, alleging that defendant day care center operators witnessed abuse of the children at a day care center and failed to report it to the police or child welfare officials. The court reversed the lower court's judgment that held defendants negligent per se for failing to report the abuse under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 261.101(a), 261.109 and overruled defendants' motion for rehearing. The court found the statute would impose liability without fault and a finding of negligence per se would result in damages disproportionate to the seriousness of the violation, a class B misdemeanor. Further, the decision to impose negligence per se could not be limited to cases charging serious misconduct, but would impose immense potential liability under an ill-defined standard on a broad class of individuals whose relationship to the abuse was extremely indirect. It was not appropriate to adopt the statute as establishing a duty and standard of conduct in tort and therefore plaintiffs could not maintain a claim for negligence per se or gross negligence based on defendants' violation of the child abuse reporting statute.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant day care center operators' motion for rehearing and reversed the lower court's judgment holding that a violation of a statutory child abuse reporting requirement was negligent per se. The court found that it was not appropriate to adopt the statute as establishing a duty and standard of conduct in tort.

 

13 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Proctor v. Andrews


No. 97-1039


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


972 S.W.2d 729; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 117; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 1172


April 1, 1998, Argued  
July 3, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE SEVENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.

This Opinion Substituted on Overrule of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 5, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. LEXIS 88.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner officers appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals for the Seventh District of Texas which held that Tex. Loc. Gov't § 143.057(d) violated the Texas Constitution in favor of respondent city.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner officers appealed a decision, which found that Tex. Loc. Gov't § 143.057(d) violated the Texas Constitution. Section 143.057(d) provided for the American Arbitration Association (AAA) or the Federal Mediation and Conciliation Service (FMCS) to provide a list of arbitrators if the parties could not agree on a hearing examiner to handle an officer's disciplinary appeal. The court held that this did not violate the authority granted to home rule cities because it was clear that the legislature intended to prevent cities from requiring the appeals to be heard only by civil service commissions. The court found the delegation to determine which arbitrators were qualified and neutral and was not overly broad because the process provided the parties with adequate participation. Neither the AAA nor the FMCS were involved in making rules, had authority to impose criminal sanctions, or had a private interest at stake. Further, the legislature did not need to set forth requirements on determining which arbitrators were qualified and neutral if those terms provided AAA and FMCS sufficient guidance.


OUTCOME: The court overruled petitioner officers' motion for rehearing and reversed the decision of the appellate court, which found that that the local government rule violated the Texas Constitution. The court reinstated the judgment rendered earlier by the trial court which compelled respondent city to comply with the local government rule.

Patterson v. Planned Parenthood


No. 97-0889


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


971 S.W.2d 439; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 104; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 1001


February 4, 1998, Argued  
June 23, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Vacated trial court's judgment and dismissed this case for want of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of health and officials brought a direct appeal of a judgment in favor of appellee family planning service provider from the 250th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), which declared a rider to appellants' biennial family planning appropriation to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state department of health and officials brought a direct appeal seeking the reversal of a judgment that declared a rider to appellants' family planning appropriation to be unconstitutional. The court vacated the judgment and dismissed the case for want of jurisdiction because the challenge by appellee family planning service provider was not ripe for review. The court determined that appellee's alleged injury remained contingent because appellee could not show a conflict between federal and state demands or that appellants' proposed action would cause any injury to appellee.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment against appellant state department of health and dismissed the case for want of jurisdiction because appellee family planning service provider's challenge was not ripe for review.

 

15 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Owens-Corning Fiberglas Corp. v. Malone


No. 96-0287, No. 96-0512


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


972 S.W.2d 35; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 97; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 877; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,274


November 21, 1996, Argued  
June 5, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIRST DISTRICT OF TEXAS. ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Owens-Corning Fiberglas Corp. v. Wasiak, 917 S.W.2d 883, 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 587 (Tex. App. Austin, 1996)
Owens-Corning Fiberglas Corp. v. Malone, 916 S.W.2d 551, 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 41 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant manufacturer petitioned for review of judgments of the Court of Appeals for the First District of Texas and the Third District of Texas that affirmed trial court judgments awarding punitive damages, arguing that the trial courts erred in excluding evidence in mitigation of punitive damages and that the awards, when aggregated with prior punitive damage awards, violated constitutional due process requirements.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed suits against defendant manufacturer for asbestos-related injuries. Defendant appealed judgments awarding punitive damages and thereafter petitioned for further review, arguing that the trial courts erred in rejecting evidence to mitigate punitive damages and that the awards, when aggregated with prior punitive damages awarded for the same conduct, violated the due process requirements of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. In affirming the lower court decisions, the court concluded that evidence of the profitability of defendant's misconduct and previously paid punitive damages for the same course of conduct was admissible to mitigate punitive damages. While this evidence should have been admitted, any error in excluding it was harmless. Further, defendant failed to establish that aggregate punitive damage awards violated substantive due process rights. Considering defendant's conduct, plaintiffs' injuries, defendant's stable finances, and punitive damages actually for the same conduct, the punitive damages awards at issue, when aggregated with prior awards, were not grossly excessive and beyond the legitimate interests of punishment and deterrence.


OUTCOME: The appellant court judgments affirming punitive damage awards were affirmed, as any error in excluding evidence mitigating punitive damages was harmless. Further, aggregated punitive damage awards for defendant manufacturer's same course of conduct did not constitute a violation of substantive due process rights where the aggregate amount was not grossly excessive and beyond the legitimate interests of punishment and deterrence.

 

16 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Appraisal Review Bd. v. Tex-Air Helicopters


No. 97-0404


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


970 S.W.2d 530; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 90; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 920


December 3, 1997, Argued  
June 5, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FOURTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tax authorities applied for a writ of error to the Court of Appeals for the Fourteenth District (Texas), which reversed a trial court judgment that found Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 21.05 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner tax authorities sought to assess helicopters that belonged to respondent air transporter at full market value. Respondent challenged the assessment, asserting that petitioner did not allocate value as required by Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 21.05. The trial court rendered summary judgment for petitioner, finding the statute to be an unconstitutional tax exemption. The court of appeals reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The supreme court affirmed the court of appeals, finding that § 21.05 could not be an unconstitutional exemption in any case in which the United States Constitution would require fair apportionment. The supreme court found that the United States Constitution limited petitioner's power to tax property which had acquired a tax situs outside the state. The supreme court determined that the facts established that the helicopters had a taxable situs in another state and, therefore, allocation was constitutionally required. Because allocation required under the United States Constitution was not an unauthorized tax exemption, the supreme court held that § 21.05 was not facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that reversed a trial court decision for petitioner tax authority, which held that a statute requiring allocation of ad valorem taxes was unconstitutional. The court held that the statute requiring allocation was not an unconstitutional unauthorized tax exemption where the United States Constitution required apportionment for property that acquired a tax situs outside the taxing authority.

In re Barr


Inquiry No. 67


REVIEW TRIBUNAL OF TEXAS


13 S.W.3d 525; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 34



February 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Rehearing of March 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1416.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State Commission on Judicial Conduct (Texas), recommended that respondent be removed as a judge and that he be prohibited from holding judicial office in the future. Respondent rejected the findings, conclusions, and recommendations of petitioner and challenged the findings and ultimate recommendation that he be removed from office.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner agency recommended that respondent judge be removed his position and that he be prohibited from holding judicial office in the future. Respondent rejected the findings and recommendations of petitioner and challenged the findings and ultimate recommendation that he be removed from office. The court found that respondent's actions constituted intentional and willful conduct. Respondent's actions were violative of Tex. Code Jud. Conduct, Canons 3B(3), (4), and (6), were clearly inconsistent with the proper performance of his duties, cast public discredit upon the judiciary of the state as well as on the administration of justice and thus were likewise violative of Tex. Const. art. V, § 1-a(6)A. The court stated that respondent's right to insult and demean was necessarily outweighed by the public interest to demand dignity. Respondent's actions were done with gross indifference to his conduct. He clearly intended to engage in conduct for which he was disciplined. The court accepted the recommendation that respondent be removed as a judge; however, the court rejected that portion of the recommendation which would forever ban respondent from holding judicial office.


OUTCOME: The court accepted petitioner agency's recommendation that respondent judge be removed from his position; however, the court rejected that portion of the recommendation which would forever ban respondent from holding judicial office. Respondent's actions were inconsistent with the proper performance of his duties and cast public discredit upon the judiciary of the state as well as on the administration of justice.

In re Lowery


Inquiry Concerning A Judge, No. 71


REVIEW TRIBUNAL OF TEXAS


999 S.W.2d 639; 1998 Tex. LEXIS 174



February 13, 1998, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed. Bill R. Lowery removed as Justice of the Peace, Precinct 2, Place 2, Irving, Dallas County, Texas, and forever barred from holding judicial office.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent justice of the peace petitioned the Texas Review Tribunal to reject the recommendation of the commission, the Texas State Commission on Judicial Conduct, for his removal and prohibition from holding judicial office in the future.


OVERVIEW: The Texas State Commission on Judicial Conduct (commission) adopted a special master's report concluding that respondent justice of the peace engaged in judicial misconduct by engaging in willful or persistent conduct that was clearly inconsistent with the proper performance of his duties, and willfully violated the Texas Code of Judicial Conduct. Respondent petitioned the Texas Review Tribunal (tribunal) to reject the commission's recommendation for his removal and prohibition from holding judicial office. The tribunal affirmed the commission's findings, conclusion, and recommendation, removed respondent, and barred respondent from holding judicial office. Respondent failed to obtain required judicial training and solicited a false report that he had. Respondent refused to pay a parking lot attendant for parking and used a racial slur. Respondent confronted one defendant outside his courtroom, held him in contempt, and fined him. Further, respondent persistently used profane and rude language.


OUTCOME: The Texas Review Tribunal affirmed the findings, conclusion, and recommendation of the Texas State Commission on Judicial Conduct, removed respondent justice of the peace, and barred respondent from holding judicial office. Three incidents directly supported the finding that respondent engaged in judicial misconduct by engaging in willful or persistent conduct that was clearly inconsistent with the proper performance of his duties.

20 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Board of Trustees v. Toungate


No. 96-0690


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


958 S.W.2d 365; 1997 Tex. LEXIS 109; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 48


April 24, 1997, Argued  
October 23, 1997, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school trustees sought review by application for writ of error from the Court of Appeals for the Third District of Texas, of its affirmance of a modified judgment that held appellant's hair-length regulation that applied only to male students violated the Texas Equal Rights Amendment, Tex. Const. art. I, § 3a, and Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 106.001(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellee student was suspended from school for having a rat tail haircut that violated appellant school trustees' hair-length regulation that applied only to male students. Appellant challenged the affirmance of a modified judgment that held the regulation violated the Texas Equal Rights Amendment, Tex. Const. art. I, § 3a, and Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 106.001(a)(4)-(6). The court reversed. Constitutional challenges to hair length regulations were nonjusticiable, and did not violate any constitutional rights. The court statutorily construed Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 106.001, and concluded that the statute's language "because of sex" was never meant to encompass grooming and dress regulations. The fact that § 106.001 imposed criminal penalties weighed heavily against construing it to prohibit the enforcing of dress and grooming codes. Section 106.001 prohibited discriminatory practices that affected the access of one sex to state benefits, amenities, or opportunities enjoyed by the other sex. Hair-length regulations in schools did not elevate one sex over the other or deny educational opportunities because of sex.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the affirmance of a modified judgment in a favor of appellee student, and held that appellant school trustees' hair-length regulation that applied only to male students neither violated a statute that precluded discrimination on the basis of sex, nor violated any constitutional rights.

Texas Boll Weevil Eradication Found. v. Lewellen


No. 96-0745 - consolidated for oral argument with - NO. 96-0839


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


952 S.W.2d 454; 1997 Tex. LEXIS 108; 41 Tex. Sup. J. 29


November 20, 1996, Argued  
October 9, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 952 S.W.2d 454 at 503.


PRIOR HISTORY: (No. 96-0745). ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 242ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HALE COUNTY, TEXAS.

(NO. 96-0839). ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 138TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT.

Original Opinion of April 30, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tex. LEXIS 48.
Texas Boll Weevil Eradication Found. v. Lewellen, 952 S.W.2d 454, 1997 Tex. LEXIS 48, 40 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 523 (Tex., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Appellant's motions for rehearing are overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant foundation moved for rehearing of its unsuccessful appeal from the judgments of the 242nd Judicial District of Hale County (Texas) and the 138th Judicial District Court of Cameron County (Texas), arguing that the court's invalidation of assessments against plaintiff farmers, made under Tex. Agric. Code Ann. § 74.101 et seq. (1993), should have prospective application only, such that refunds would not be owed for past assessments.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff farmers brought suit in two courts against defendant foundation to invalidate certain assessments made against them under Tex. Agric. Code Ann. § 74.101 et seq. (1993). Plaintiffs claimed that the statute and assessments were unconstitutional. Judgment in both cases was entered for plaintiffs and defendant appealed, but the judgment invalidating the statute and assessments was affirmed. In response to the court's opinion, the legislature amended the statutory scheme at issue. Defendant then moved for a rehearing, asserting that the decision should apply to future assessments only, that is, it should not have retroactive application, such that defendant would have to pay refunds for past assessments. In overruling the motions for rehearing, the court ruled that, despite the general rule that decisions applied retroactively, because the law had been modified, the appropriate forum for any challenge was in the trial courts and not on motion for rehearing.


OUTCOME: The motions for rehearing were overruled because, in response to the original judgment of the court, the legislature had modified the applicable statutory law, such that any challenge to the law was in the appropriate trial courts.

 

22 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Federal Sign v. Texas S. Univ.


No. 94-1317


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


951 S.W.2d 401; 1997 Tex. LEXIS 58; 40 Tex. Sup. J. 676


November 28, 1995, Argued  
June 20, 1997, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FOURTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner business challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals for the Fourteenth District of Texas, which reversed the trial court judgment in favor of petitioner and remanded the case with instructions to dismiss because respondent state university's plea to the jurisdiction based upon sovereign immunity should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: The lower court determined that the trial court should have sustained respondent state university's plea to the jurisdiction based upon sovereign immunity. Petitioner business challenged the lower court decision, claiming that legislative consent to sue was not necessary because respondent violated state laws, that respondent waived immunity by entering into a contract with a private citizen, and that sovereign immunity from contract claims violated the Texas Constitution's open courts and due course of law provisions. Affirming the lower court's judgment, the court held that petitioner's breach of contract claim for monetary damages required legislative consent, notwithstanding the allegation that there were related state law violations. The court also held that by entering into contracts with private citizens, the state waived only immunity from liability, not from suit, so a private citizen needed to obtain legislative consent to sue the state for breach. Finally, the court held that sovereign immunity did not deny petitioner due process, because relief was available to petitioner by seeking the legislature's consent to sue, and it held that the open courts claim was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court dismissing petitioner business' suit against respondent state university, holding that sovereign immunity from suit without legislative consent applied to claims for damages for breach of contract against the state, even if related state law violations were alleged, and this application did not violate either the open courts or the due course of law provisions of the Texas Constitution.

Texas Boll Weevil Eradication Found. v. Lewellen


No. 96-0745 - consolidated for oral argument with - No. 96-0839


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


952 S.W.2d 454; 1997 Tex. LEXIS 48; 40 Tex. Sup. J. 523


November 20, 1996, Argued  
April 30, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Supplemental Opinion on Rehearing Overruled October 9, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tex. LEXIS 108.
Rehearing overruled by, Supplemental opinion at Texas Boll Weevil Eradication Found. v. Lewellen, 952 S.W.2d 454, 1997 Tex. LEXIS 108, 41 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 29 (Tex., 1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 242ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HALE COUNTY, TEXAS (No. 96-0745).

ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 138TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF CAMERON COUNTY, TEXAS (No. 96-0839).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foundation challenged, in a consolidated action, the declaratory judgments from the 242nd Judicial District Court of Hale County (Texas), and the 138th Judicial District Court of Cameron County (Texas), which invalidated appellant's assessments under Tex. Agric. Code Ann. §§ 74.101-.127 (1993) on appellee cotton growers as violative of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13; art. VIII, § 1(c); and art. II, § 1, and enjoined their collection.


OVERVIEW: Appellee cotton growers filed declaratory judgment actions challenging appellant foundation's assessments under the Official Cotton Growers' Boll Weevil Eradication Foundation Act (Act), Tex. Agric. Code Ann. §§ 74.101-.127 (1993). Appellees' actions were based on a variety of constitutional and statutory grounds. The trial courts invalidated the assessments and enjoined their collection. Appellant sought immediate review with the Texas supreme court. The court held that the assessments constituted regulatory fees rather than taxes, and were not taxes on an agricultural pursuit in violation of Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1(c). The court further held that the Act, on its face and as applied to appellees, did not violate the right to equal protection under Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court applied an eight-part test and determined that the Act represented an overly broad delegation of legislative authority to a private entity. Thus, the court affirmed the judgments of the trial courts because the legislature made an unconstitutionally broad delegation of authority to appellant, a private entity, thereby violating the separation of power clause, Tex. Const. art. II, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgments of the trial courts because the legislature made an unconstitutionally broad delegation of authority under the Official Cotton Growers' Boll Weevil Eradication Foundation Act to appellant foundation, a private entity, and thereby violated the state constitutional separation of powers clause.

Diaz v. Westphal

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor applied for a writ of error after the Court of Appeals for the Thirteenth District of Texas reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellant, alleging that appellee wife of decedent's wrongful death and survival action asserted on behalf of her minor son was not filed within the applicable statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellee wife of decedent brought a medical malpractice suit against appellant doctor on her behalf, as well as on the behalf of her minor son. The trial court rendered summary judgment for appellant doctor holding that the suit was not timely filed. A divided court of appeals reversed and remanded decedent's minor son's claim for trial. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals because it found decedent's minor son's claim was derivative of the decedent's medical malpractice claim. Because decedent did not file a medical malpractice action before he died, his minor son's claim under the medical malpractice statute was barred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and held that, because limitations barred the decedent's common-law action because he did not file it before he died, his son's derivative wrongful death claim was also barred.

Central Power & Light Co. v. Sharp


No. 96-0621


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


960 S.W.2d 617; 1997 Tex. LEXIS 34; 40 Tex. Sup. J. 443



March 21, 1997, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Application for Writ of Error Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a tax refund suit, petitioner company sought an application for writ of error to the Court of Appeals for the Third District (Texas), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondent comptroller.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner company filed a tax refund suit in district court, seeking judicial review of respondent comptroller's order on numerous grounds, including that Tex. Tax Code § 171.109(b) violated the Tex. Const. art. III, § 1 prohibition against delegation of legislative power to outside authority. Petitioner contended that § 171.109(b) unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority to a private entity. The district court granted respondent's motion for summary judgment and the appellate court affirmed. Petitioner filed an application for writ of error. The court denied petitioner's application. The court held that the court of appeals correctly stated the general rule that the grounds of error contained in the motion for rehearing before the agency were the only issues that may be raised in a suit seeking a refund of taxes paid. However, the court of appeals ignored an exception to this rule. Petitioner's challenge of respondent comptroller's order, on the ground that the underlying statute was unconstitutional, was within the trial court's jurisdiction even though petitioner did not raise the constitutional challenge in its motion for rehearing before the agency.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner company's application for writ of error, holding that petitioner company's challenge of respondent comptroller's order, on the ground that the underlying statute was unconstitutional, was within the trial court's jurisdiction even though petitioner did not raise the constitutional challenge in its motion for rehearing before the agency.

Maple Run at Austin Mun. Util. Dist. v. Monaghan


No. 96-0489


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


931 S.W.2d 941; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 153; 40 Tex. Sup. J. 54


September 4, 1996, Argued  
October 18, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 53RD DISTRICT COURT, TRAVIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility district sought review of the judgment of the 53rd District Court of Travis County (Texas), in favor of appellees landowners and city that declared the Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code Ann. § 43.082, which permitted annexation of the district without notice and hearing procedures, unconstitutional and permanently enjoined its operation.


OVERVIEW: The lower court agreed with appellees landowners and city and entered judgment that Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code Ann. § 43.082, which permitted dissolution of the utility district, annexation of it without notice and hearing procedures, and required the city to take ownership of the district's assets and assume its debts, unconstitutional and permanently enjoined its operation. Appellant district sought review of the lower court's judgment and the court affirmed the judgment and held that Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code Ann. § 43.082 was not authorized under Tex. Const. art XVI, § 59, and therefore was a prohibited local law under Tex. Const. art. III, § 56. The court held that the statute was a local law within the meaning of Tex. Const. art. III, § 56 because it singled out one specific municipal utility district for special treatment without any reasonable basis for doing so. The court found that in every other instance examined, the legislature either determined there was no outstanding indebtedness, required a plan to liquidate its indebtedness, or conditioned dissolution on a city's consent, while this statute required the city to assume assets and indebtedness without their consent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and held that Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code Ann. § 43.082 was not authorized under Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 59, and therefore was a prohibited local law under Tex. Const. art. III, § 56, because it singled out one specific municipal utility district for special treatment without any reasonable basis for doing so.

State ex rel. Angelini v. Hardberger


No. 96-0643


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


932 S.W.2d 489; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 134; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 1084


August 13, 1996, Argued On  
August 30, 1996, Delivered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator filed an original petition for emergency writ of quo warranto seeking a declaration that respondent, Justice of the Court of Appeals for the Fourth District of Texas, had vacated his office and that there was a vacancy therefore to be filled.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Court of Appeals Justice submitted his resignation from his position effective on a date certain which was six months away from the date of the resignation. The Governor appointed relator to fill the unexpired term, however, respondent refused to vacate his position. Relator filed a petition for a writ of quo warranto seeking to force respondent to vacate his office arguing that Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 201.023 provides that resignations are effective on the date the resignation is accepted or the eighth day after the date of its receipt. The court rejected this argument noting that the Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 17 allows for a period of service for a justice to be extended, but not truncated. The court held that, because the effective date of respondent's resignation is the actual date he would leave office for that term if he did not seek reelection, he would only vacate his office in the constitutional sense on that date. The court therefore denied the writ of quo warranto.


OUTCOME: Relator's petition for writ of quo warranto seeking to compel respondent Justice to vacate his office before the effective date of his resignation was denied because the state constitution did not provide for his period of service to be truncated.

Tilton v. Marshall


No. 94-1233


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


925 S.W.2d 672; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 111; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 985


March 21, 1995, Argued  
July 12, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Relators' Motion for Rehearing In Part for Withdrawn Opinion of August 1, 1995; Previously Reported at: 1995 Tex. LEXIS 140.



DISPOSITION: Relators' motion for rehearing granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, pastor and churches, filed a petition for writ of mandamus with the court, which requested the court to reverse respondent trial court's discovery order and to dismiss plaintiffs' causes of action against relators on grounds that relators' rights were violated under U.S. Const. amend. I, Tex. Const. art. I, § 6, and the Religious Freedom Restoration Act of 1993, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb-bb4.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against relators, pastor and churches, that alleged fraud, conspiracy, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. Respondent trial court entered a discovery order that required relators to produce tithing records. Relators petitioned for a writ of mandamus that sought reversal of the discovery order and dismissal of the claims based on U.S. Const. amend. I, Tex. Const. art. I, § 6, and the Religious Freedom Restoration Act of 1993, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb-bb4. The court reversed the discovery order and dismissed the emotional distress claim, but permitted the fraud claim to proceed. The fraud and conspiracy claims based on the relators' failure to read plaintiffs' prayer requests as promised were constitutional because the claims were based on the promise to perform particular acts. The jury was not permitted to determine the truth or falsity of relators' allegedly fraudulent statements of religious belief or doctrine. The intentional infliction of emotional distress and related conspiracy claims required an unconstitutional inquiry into the truth or falsity of relators' religious beliefs. The discovery order was no longer relevant.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted relators', pastor and churches, writ of mandamus against respondent trial court as to relators' allegedly fraudulent statements of religious belief and plaintiffs' claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress because the claims violated the constitutional right to the free exercise of religion. The fraud claims for relators' failure to perform specified acts as promised were constitutional.

Barshop v. Medina County Underground Water Conservation Dist.


No. 95-0881


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


925 S.W.2d 618; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 81; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 858


March 20, 1996, Argued  
June 28, 1996, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 38TH DISTRICT COURT OF MEDINA COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: District court's judgment reversed; judgment rendered in favor of the State; Cause remanded to the district court to exercise its discretion as to whether attorney's fees should be awarded to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants state, city, and directors appealed from the judgment of the 38th District Court of Medina County (Texas) that enjoined implementation of the Edwards Aquifer Act (Act), 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 2353, upon declaring that the Act facially violated several provisions of the Texas Constitution and infringed upon the rights of plaintiff challengers to withdraw water from beneath their own property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challengers brought a facial challenge to the validity of the Edwards Aquifer Act (Act), 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 2353, under various provisions of the Texas Constitution. Plaintiffs claimed the law violated their property rights to obtain underground water from their own property, while defendants state, city, and directors asserted it merely regulated groundwater resources for conservation purposes by imposing caps on well withdrawals and imposing a permit system that gave preference to existing users. The trial court declared the Act unconstitutional and enjoined its implementation. Defendants appealed. In reversing, the court ruled that the Act was presumed to be constitutional and plaintiffs failed to meet their burden of showing that the Act would always operate unconstitutionally. The law was properly enacted pursuant to constitutional notice requirements and it did not permit the taking of private property without adequate compensation. Moreover, the Act did not violate state constitutional provisions pertaining to equal protection, due course of law, retroactive laws, obligation of contracts, separation of powers, open courts, or right to jury trial.


OUTCOME: The declaratory judgment of facial invalidity was reversed and the injunction was dissolved because plaintiffs failed to show that the law was unconstitutional in all possible applications; the statute was validly enacted; it was not a taking of property without due compensation or improper retroactive law; and it did not violate equal protection, due course of law, separation of powers, or the right to trial by jury.

 

33 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Saenz v. Fidelity & Guar. Ins. Underwriters


No. D-4561


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


925 S.W.2d 607; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 68; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 743


November 15, 1994, Argued  
June 14, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the lower courts reversed and judgment rendered that Saenz take nothing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a workers' compensation claimant and his wife, appealed a judgment from the Thirteenth District Court of Appeals (Texas) affirming an award of mental anguish damages for fraud and punitive damages against respondent insurance adjuster, but reversing an award of punitive damages against respondent insurance company and reversing an award for future medical expenses.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant was injured on the job and entered into a compromise settlement agreement. Months later, petitioner discovered that she may have been fraudulently induced to enter into the agreement by respondent insurance company and respondent individual. The jury found that petitioner was fraudulently induced and awarded damages for mental anguish, future medical costs, and punitive damages. The court of appeals affirmed as to the award of damages for mental anguish, but reversed as to the award of punitive damages and future medical expenses. The court reversed and ordered that petitioner take nothing. Petitioner could not recover the value of the benefits she would have been entitled to but for the settlement; her sole remedy was rescission of the settlement agreement and reassertion of her claim. Additionally, petitioner failed to meet the threshold showing of mental anguish where the only evidence presented was that she was worried, anxious and angry. Because she was not entitled to actual damages, it followed that petitioner was not entitled to punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and petitioners were ordered to take nothing because petitioner claimant's sole remedy for loss of medical benefits based on fraud was rescission of the compromise settlement agreement, petitioner failed to show mental anguish, and petitioner was not entitled to punitive damages.

 

34 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Central Appraisal Dist. v. Lall


No. 95-0710 - consolidated with - No. 95-0717


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


924 S.W.2d 686; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 69; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 762


December 13, 1995, Argued  
June 14, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATIONS FOR WRITS OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIFTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the court of appeals modified and causes remanded to the trial courts for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Fifth District Court of Appeals (Texas) finding that the forfeiture provision of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08 was unconstitutional and violated respondent's right to open courts pursuant to Tex. Const. art. I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed respondent's action challenging the assessment of an ad valorem tax due to respondent's failure to tender partial payment under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08. The statute provided that a taxpayer forfeited the right to judicial review of an assessment unless the taxpayer paid either the amount of taxes due on that portion of the taxable value of the property not in dispute or the amount of taxes imposed on the property for the preceding year. The court of appeals reversed, finding that the statute impeded respondent's right to open courts in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court affirmed the reversal. That part of the statute requiring payment of the undisputed portion was constitutional in light of the importance that local governments have a steady revenue stream. However, that part of the statute requiring payment of the preceding year's tax assessment and requiring a taxpayer to pay any portion of the disputed amount, imposed an unreasonable financial barrier to court access.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding that the forfeiture provision of the tax code was unconstitutional was affirmed because the statute facially violated the open courts provision of the state constitution in requiring a taxpayer to pay a disputed amount of a tax assessment as a condition to judicial review.

 

35 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Harris County Appraisal Dist. v. Herrin


No. 96-0371


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


924 S.W.2d 154; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 73; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 787



June 14, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FOURTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: HCAD's application for writ of error granted; Judgment of the court of appeals modified; Remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appraisal district and board sought a writ of error from a judgment from the Court of Appeals for the Fourteenth District of Texas holding that Tex. Tax Code § 42.08 was unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The lower court affirmed the denial of petitioners' motion for summary judgment alleging respondent taxpayers' suit should be dismissed because they did not pay taxes before the delinquency date pursuant to § 42.08.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners appraisal board and district sought a writ of error from the lower court's judgment concluding that Tex. Tax Code § 42.08 was unconstitutional under the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court granted the writ, modified the lower court's judgment and remanded to the trial court. The court held that only one prong of § 42.08 was unconstitutional under the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court held that § 42.08 violated a taxpayer's right to open courts only when applied to the prong of § 42.08 that required a taxpayer to pay the amount of taxes imposed in the preceding year before the delinquency date or risk forfeiture of the right to judicial review of an ad valorem tax assessment. The court, however, held that respondent taxpayers were still required to pay any undisputed taxes before the delinquency date pursuant to § 42.08. Respondents failed to pay any taxes prior to the delinquency date, and therefore, they forfeited their right to maintain a suit. The court remanded to the trial court to determine whether any special terms and conditions should be imposed under the circumstances pursuant to § 42.08(d).


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners' writ of error, modified the lower court's judgment, and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The court held that only part of the forfeiture statute was unconstitutional under the open courts provision of the state constitution. Respondent taxpayers failed to pay the undisputed taxes before the delinquency date, and as such, they forfeited their right to maintain judicial review of an assessment.

 

36 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Travelers Indem. Co. v. Mayfield


No. 95-1209


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


923 S.W.2d 590; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 63; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 678


April 17, 1996, Argued  
May 31, 1996, Delivered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the workers' compensation proceeding underlying the original mandamus proceeding, the trial court appointed an attorney to represent the claimant, ordering relator carrier to pay opposing counsel's fees as the case progressed. While not challenging the appointment itself, relator contended that the trial court abused its discretion and caused irreparable harm by requiring it to pay for the claimant's attorney.


OVERVIEW: Relator carrier brought a mandamus proceeding. In underlying workers' compensation action, the trial court appointed an attorney to represent the claimant, ordering the relator to pay opposing counsel's fees. The relator contended the trial court abused its discretion by requiring it to pay the claimant's attorney. The court agreed. Attorney fees could not be recovered from an opposing party unless such recovery was provided for by statute or by contract. The authorization of attorney fees could not be inferred; rather it must be provided for by the express terms of the statute. There was no statute which authorized recovery of attorney fees under the circumstances. Further, the Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 24.016 vested judges with discretion to appoint counsel for indigent litigants, but did not authorize judges to shift the fees for appointed counsel to the opposing party. Because the authority for a fee award could not be supplied by implication but must be provided for by express terms of the statute, the court could not construe Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 24.016 as impliedly authorizing a trial court to place the financial burden of appointed counsel on the opposing party.


OUTCOME: The writ of mandamus of relator carrier was conditionally granted. The court concluded that the trial court, having appointed an attorney to represent the claimant, could not require the relator to pay the fees for that attorney. Placing this burden on the relator constituted an abuse of discretion.

 

37 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Medina v. Herrera


No. 95-0885


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


927 S.W.2d 597; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 55


December 12, 1995, Argued  
May 10, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FOURTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of the judgment on a writ of error to the Court of Appeals for the Fourteenth District of Texas, which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondents, employer and supervisor, because the employee elected to obtain benefits under the Texas Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 401.001-418.002.


OVERVIEW: The employee received workers' compensation benefits when his supervisor assaulted him, causing him to fall and injure his back. The employee also filed an intentional tort claim against respondents. The lower appellate court held that workers' compensation and common law intentional tort remedies were mutually exclusive as against both respondents. On appeal, the court found that the employee's claim for workers' compensation and his intentional tort claim against the employer were mutually exclusive. Additionally, manifest injustice would result if the employee were permitted to maintain his intentional tort action against the employer. If the assault was motivated by an employment-related dispute or directly attributable to the employer, then the Act provided the employee's exclusive remedy under Tex. Lab. Code § 408.001. If the assault was unrelated to the employment, then the employer was not vicariously liable for the supervisor's intentional misconduct. However, the employee's intentional tort claim against the supervisor could be maintained because the Act was not intended to shield the supervisor from liability for his own intentional assault on the employee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the employer but reversed the grant of summary judgment to the supervisor. The court remanded the action for further proceedings.

H.E. Butt Grocery Co. v. Jefferson County Appraisal Dist.


No. 95-1218


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


922 S.W.2d 941; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 47



May 10, 1996, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE NINTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer applied for a writ of error to the Court of Appeals for the Ninth District of Texas, which held that Tex. Tax Code § 23.12(f) (1989) violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1(a) as applied to petitioner's inventory in its general grocery store acquired after September 1, 1991 in favor of respondent Jefferson County Appraisal District.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.12(f) (1989), petitioner taxpayer elected to have all of its inventory located in respondent Jefferson County Appraisal District's area appraised for 1992 ad valorem tax purposes at market value as of September 1, 1991. Petitioner listed both grocery store and video store inventory. Respondent denied petitioner's application as to inventory that petitioner acquired after September 1, 1991 for its new store sites. Petitioner filed a petition for review of respondent's valuation and the court of appeals held that § 23.12(f) was unconstitutional as applied to the inventory. The court reversed and held that § 23.12(f) did not result in an unconstitutional exemption of property simply because the volume and value of petitioner's inventory increased after the September 1 valuation date. The court also held that that § 23.12(f) was not an exemption from taxation, but rather a provision for an alternative valuation date that was not unreasonably arbitrary or capricious. Additionally, the court held that § 23.12(f) did not violate Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1(a).


OUTCOME: On petitioner taxpayer's writ of error, the court reversed the judgment that the provision of the Texas Tax Code allowing petitioner to elect an alternative valuation date for appraisal of its inventory acquired after September 1, 1991 by respondent Jefferson County Appraisal District did not violate the Texas Constitution.

Enron Corp. v. Spring Indep. Sch. Dist.

S.V. v. R.V.


No. 94-0856


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


933 S.W.2d 1; 1996 Tex. LEXIS 30; 39 Tex. Sup. J. 386


February 8, 1995, Argued  
March 14, 1996, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Justice Coryn's Concurring Opinion Withdrawn and Substituted November 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF ERROR TO THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIFTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals of Texas, Fifth District, Dallas, which reversed an order of the trial court granting a directed verdict against respondent daughter in an action that alleged negligent sexual abuse of a child.


OVERVIEW: Respondent daughter brought an action against petitioner father that alleged negligent sexual abuse of petitioner before the age of 17. The daughter alleged that she had repressed the memories of the abuse, and brought the action as an adult after she remembered the abuse. The trial court granted a directed verdict for the daughter. The lower court reversed the trial court and remanded the cause for a new trial. The court reversed the lower court and affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the daughter's action was subject to the two-year statute of limitations which did not begin to run until her eighteenth birthday, but she brought her action more than four months after the limitations period had expired. The court held that the discovery rule, which tolled the statute of limitations until the discovery of the cause of action, was not applicable to the daughter because there was no physical or other evidence to satisfy the element of objective verifiability for application of the discovery rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court that reversed a directed verdict in favor of the father in a negligent sexual abuse of a child case was reversed and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the daughter's action was barred by the statute of limitations and the discovery rule for tolling the statute did not apply.
