PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator candidate challenged a judgment of respondent Fourteenth Court of Appeals (Texas), which granted a writ of mandamus to remove relator's name from the Democratic primary ballot.


OVERVIEW: Relator candidate was the sole candidate in the Democratic primary for a position as an appeals court justice. The sole candidate in the Republican primary filed an original mandamus action in the court of appeals to compel the removal of relator's name from the Democratic primary ballot, alleging that relator's petitions did not comply with Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 141.062, 141.063, and 141.065 because they did not have at least 250 signatures by registered voters. The court of appeals issued the writ of mandamus to remove relator's name from the primary ballot because it concluded that she only had 247 valid signatures. Relator appealed the decision, and the court held that the court of appeals abused its discretion by adjudicating constitutional issues that necessarily dealt with disputed areas of fact. The court found that the issues raised in the case required factual determinations that the court of appeals could not properly have made in an original mandamus proceeding, and conditionally entered a writ of mandamus directing the court of appeals to withdraw its writ.


OUTCOME: The court held that the court of appeals abused its discretion in granting the writ of mandamus to remove relator candidate's name from the ballot because it decided constitutional issues that dealt with disputed areas of fact. The court conditionally issued a writ of mandamus directing the court of appeals to withdraw its writ and any related orders, and overruled the motion for rehearing.

 

114 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


General Land Office v. OXY U.S.A., Inc.


No. C-9289


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


789 S.W.2d 569; 1990 Tex. LEXIS 72; 33 Tex. Sup. J. 488



May 16, 1990, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

DIRECT APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The General Land Office of the State of Texas (GLO) filed a direct appeal of the trial court's temporary injunction of GLO's proceedings against appellee oil company. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss the underlying cause without prejudice and the trial court dismissed the case. The issue for the court was whether the direct appeal should be dismissed because the controversy on which it was based was rendered moot.


OVERVIEW: Appellee oil company filed suit to enjoin the General Land Office of the State of Texas (GLO) from conducting hearings regarding appellee's rights under certain oil and gas leases. The trial court found that the GLO's statutory right to adjudicate lease obligations violated the Texas Constitution and enjoined the proceedings against appellee. The GLO filed a notice of accelerated direct appeal and appellee filed a motion requesting that the underlying cause be dismissed without prejudice. Finding that the GLO sought no affirmative relief that would defeat the motion, the trial court dismissed the cause. The court found that the trial court had correctly granted the nonsuit. When the underlying action was dismissed, the temporary injunction dissolved automatically. The court held that the controversy was moot and dismissed the cause.


OUTCOME: The court held that the direct appeal had to be dismissed because the underlying cause was moot. The trial court's grant of a nonsuit was correct and as a result the temporary injunction ceased to exist and the appeal became moot.

 

115 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brady v. Fourteenth Court of Appeals


No. C-9538


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


1990 Tex. LEXIS 41; 33 Tex. Sup. J. 358



March 28, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Overruled and Opinion Withdrawn June 20, 1990; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1990 Tex. LEXIS 95.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, candidate for election, sought a writ of mandamus directing respondent, the Fourteenth Court of Appeals (Texas), to withdraw the writ of mandamus it issued in an original proceeding brought by relator's opposition, which directed that relator's name be removed from the election ballot.


OVERVIEW: Relator, candidate for election, had her name removed from the election ballot through a writ of mandamus issued by the appeals court in response to a petition by relator's opposition. Relator then sought this writ of mandamus directing the appeals court to withdraw its writ. The court held that the resolution of the issues presented to the appeals court required factual determinations that could not properly be made by an appellate court in an original proceeding. The appeals court should not have decided factual questions on inconsistent and conflicting affidavits. In addition, when a political party questions the constitutionality of state statutes regulating the party's method of selecting a candidate, the rights secured by the U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV are implicated and the courts must employ a balancing test that is necessarily fact intensive. The court conditionally granted the writ holding that the appeals court abused its discretion by deciding factual issues in an original proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandamus directing respondent, appeals court, to withdraw the writ it issued in an original mandamus proceeding that directed that relator, candidate for election, be removed from the ballot and that necessarily involved the resolution of disputed factual issues.

 

116 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Moreno v. Sterling Drug, Inc.


No. C-7744


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


787 S.W.2d 348; 1990 Tex. LEXIS 43; 33 Tex. Sup. J. 360; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,427



March 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON CERTIFIED QUESTION FROM THE UNITED STATES COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIFTH CIRCUIT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit granted appellant parent's motion to certify legal questions to the court. The court considered whether the discovery rule applied to the Texas Statute of Limitations, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(b) (1986), in appellant's wrongful death action, and if the discovery rule did not apply, did the statute's application violate the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment for appellee manufacturer in appellant parent's wrongful death suit, because appellant brought the suit more than two years after his infant's date of death. Appellant argued that the discovery rule, an exception to statutes of limitations, should apply to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(b) (1986), because he neither knew nor could have known the cause of his injury within the two-year limitation period. The court found that the language used in § 16.003(b) reflected a clear legislative intent to adopt an absolute two-year limitations period for wrongful death actions and that the legislature foreclosed judicial application of the discovery rule. Appellant contended that if § 16.003(b) did not provide for application of the discovery rule, it violated the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court found that there was no recognized common law cause of action for wrongful death. The court concluded that appellant's constitutional attack of § 16.003(b) was not premised upon restriction of a common-law cause of action, and, therefore, necessarily failed the first prong of the open courts test.


OUTCOME: The court found that the discovery rule did not apply to statute of limitations for actions based on injuries resulting in death. The court found that the statute of limitations as applied to appellant parent did not violate the open courts provision of the constitution.

 

117 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Association of Texas Professional Educators v. Kirby


No. C-9155


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


788 S.W.2d 827; 1990 Tex. LEXIS 25; 33 Tex. Sup. J. 275



February 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Association of Texas Professional Educators and individual teacher, sought review from the 167th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which denied a temporary injunction in a suit challenging the constitutionality of a House Bill signed by the Governor against appellee State Commissioner of Education.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, the Association of Texas Professional Educators and individual teacher, sought an injunction against appellee State Commissioner of Education to enjoin the enforcement of House Bill 2566, which amended certain provisions of the Texas Education Code relating to the teacher career ladder system. House Bill 2566 was signed by the Governor although the bill as passed by the House of Representatives and the Senate was not the bill signed by the presiding officer of each house, nor was the bill as passed by both houses presented to the Governor for his approval. The trial court held that the "enrolled bill rule" precluded inquiry into the constitutional defects alleged by appellants. The court reversed and remanded holding that an exception to the "enrolled bill rule" applied where legislative journals and testimony showed clerical errors were made in the enrolled bill. The bill could not be severed because the interconnectedness of the provisions made it unclear whether the legislature would have enacted the bill if the section in dispute were left out.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for rendition of a temporary injunction pending final disposition of permanent injunction proceedings; official legislative journals, testimony by presiding officers of both houses, and stipulations of the attorney general acting in his official capacity showed clerical error in the enrolled bill; an exception to the enrolled bill rule applied.

 

118 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Raborn v. Davis


No. C-7910


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


1990 Tex. LEXIS 17; 33 Tex. Sup. J. 249



February 21, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Vacated June 27, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. LEXIS 101.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM HARRIS COUNTY FIRST DISTRICT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought review of a decision of the First District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found that the trial court could not order respondent client to turn over his paychecks to a receiver to satisfy a judgment rendered against him.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner attorney earned a judgment against respondent client for unpaid legal fees. When the judgment was not satisfied, he sought relief under the turnover statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 31.002 (1986). The lower court determined that the trial court could not order respondent to turn over his wages to a receiver because that would be a garnishment prohibited by Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 28. The reviewing court overturned that ruling. Garnishment necessarily involves a third party who has possession of the debtor's property or owes the debtor money. In this case, no third party was involved. The trial court ordered respondent himself to turn over property he either currently possessed or might possess in the future. Because no third party was involved, there was no garnishment.


OUTCOME: A decision that found that the trial court could not order respondent client to turn over his paychecks to a receiver to satisfy a judgment rendered against him was reversed and remanded because no third party was involved, therefore there was no garnishment.

 

119 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Meyer


No. C-9396


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


787 S.W.2d 42; 1990 Tex. LEXIS 11; 33 Tex. Sup. J. 207



February 7, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From Brazoria County, First District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a candidate for public office, sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Texas), which found that petitioner was not qualified to run for attorney general because as a mid-term legislator he had been granted an increase in retirement benefits and, therefore, his candidacy was in violation of Tex. Const. art. III, § 18 which prohibited "emoluments."


OVERVIEW: The court held that petitioner, a candidate for public office, was eligible to run for attorney general because an increase in his retirement benefits as a mid-term state legislator did not constitute an "emolument" in violation of Tex. Const. art. III, § 18. The court stated that there was no certainty that petitioner would ever receive the retirement benefits and held that retirement benefits for legislators and other elected officials did not constitute "emoluments" within the meaning of § 18 because this term meant only actual pecuniary gain and not a contingent or remote benefit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the Texas Constitution did not preclude a mid-term legislator from running for another public office where his retirement benefits had been increased. The court held that the benefits did not constitute prohibited "emoluments" under the state constitution.

Dewberry v. State


NO. 72,640


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


4 S.W.3d 735; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 115



October 20, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied May 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3459.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Jefferson County trial court (Texas), which convicted him of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 (a)(2) and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 (a)(2) and sentenced to death. Appellant raised 23 points of error. He argued that the evidence was legally insufficient to convict him of capital murder and insufficient to support his punishment. Specifically, appellant argued that there was insufficient evidence for the jury to infer future dangerousness and imposed capital punishment. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction and sentencing. At the trial, a forensic pathologist testified there were four small caliber gunshot wounds and one contact shotgun wound to the victim's head. In addition, evidence indicated that the victim was found lying on the floor in the living room, with his hands tied behind his back with a telephone cord, and his feet tied together with a belt. The court held that there was sufficient evidence for the jury to rationally infer future dangerousness from the brutality of this offense.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to rationally infer future dangerousness from the brutality of the offense, thereby supporting appellant's death sentence.

Ibarra v. State


NO. 72,974


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


11 S.W.3d 189; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 117



October 20, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5219.

Writ of certiorari denied Ibarra v. Texas, 531 U.S. 828, 121 S. Ct. 79, 148 L. Ed. 2d 41, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5219 (2000)

PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM LENNAN COUNTY.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the conviction and death sentence entered by the Lennan County Court (Texas) for appellant's crime of capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and was sentenced to death. Appellant challenged, and the court affirmed. The issuance of a second search warrant under amended Tex. The court did not need to reach the issue of whether appellant's consent was tainted because, even assuming that the trial court erred in failing to suppress the complained-of evidence, appellant was not harmed by its admission. There was no error in allowing identification testimony before the jury.


OUTCOME: The death sentence was affirmed. Appellant had no right to be free from search and seizure, only unreasonable search and seizure. Appellant's due process rights were not violated, and evidence was not improperly admitted.

Medina v. State

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


7 S.W.3d 633; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 108



October 6, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied May 1, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3084.
Writ of certiorari denied Medina v. Texas, 529 U.S. 1102, 120 S. Ct. 1840, 146 L. Ed. 2d 782, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3084 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Ex parte Medina, 2005 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 253 (Tex. Crim. App., Nov. 23, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Ex parte Medina, 2009 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 562 (Tex. Crim. App., Sept. 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM HARRIS COUNTY.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 2, 1999, Previoulsy Reported at: 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 60.
Medina v. State, 994 S.W.2d 153, 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 60, 99:31 Tex. Crim. App. Op. Serv. 3 (Tex. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of capital murder, challenged the order of the Harris County Court, Texas, which sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Appellant raised twenty-two points of error, including a challenge to the legal sufficiency of the evidence to establish an intent to kill. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentencing. The court held that appellant's act of firing bullets at human height into a home which appellant knew to be occupied supplied ample evidence for a rational jury to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant had the requisite intent to kill. Therefore, the jury's verdict was not against the great weight of the evidence, clearly wrong and unjust, or biased. The court also affirmed the trial court's denial of a jury instruction on the lesser-included offenses of felony murder and manslaughter, because there was no evidence that appellant's culpable mental state did not rise to the level of an intentional and knowing killing.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; evidence which established that appellant fired bullets into a home which he knew to be occupied was both legally and factually sufficient to establish his intent to kill.

Aguirre v. State


NO. 580-98


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


22 S.W.3d 463; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 104



September 29, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Motion for Rehearing Denied December 8, 1999. As Modified December 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON STATE'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS EL PASO COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state petitioned for discretionary review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, El Paso County (Texas), which dismissed several complaints against appellee adult business owner. The complaints alleged the adult business owner engaged in unlawful business conduct for operating a nude live entertainment club within 1,000 feet of a school in violation of El Paso City, Tex., Code § 20.08.080.


OVERVIEW: Adult business owner was convicted in municipal court of operating a nude live entertainment club within 1,000 feet of a school in violation of City of El Paso, Tex., City Code § 20.08.080. The municipal court of appeals affirmed. On further appeal, the decision was reversed and the complaint dismissed, along with the complaints in several other companion cases, because they did not allege a culpable mental state. The state petitioned for discretionary review. The court upheld the dismissal of the complaints. The court found that a culpable mental state was required for § 20.08.080, even though the ordinance did not prescribe one because the definition of the offense did not plainly dispense with any mental element. The court further held that a court must look for a manifest intent to dispense with the requirement of a culpable mental state, and that the silence of a statute about whether a culpable mental state is an element of the offense left a presumption that one was.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of complaints, finding a culpable mental state was required to find a violation of a city ordinance regulating the operation of adult businesses.

Related proceeding at Guidry v. State, 9 S.W.3d 133, 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 145 (Tex. Crim. App., 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Prystash v. Texas, 529 U.S. 1102, 120 S. Ct. 1840, 146 L. Ed. 2d 782, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3083 (2000)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by Prystash v. Quarterman, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60359 (S.D. Tex., Aug. 25, 2006)

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM HARRIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Harris County Criminal Court (Texas) convicting him of capital murder in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a) and sentencing him to death pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(g).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of murder and sentenced to die under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(g), argued that the trial court erred in excluding evidence of a plea offer of 55 years in prison, because it showed that he was not "deathworthy." The court found the evidence more prejudicial than probative under Tex. R. Evid. 403 because the different motives for the offer would confuse the jury. Appellant also argued that the trial court erred in omitting an instruction about the nature of his involvement in the crime, but the court rejected that argument because appellant requested the omission. The court found that there was no burden of proof as to victim impact evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that evidence of an offer of 55 years in prison was prejudicial because motives behind it were confusing, that appellant could not raise jury instruction omission as error when he requested it, and that there was no burden of proof for victim impact evidence.

Reynolds v. State


NO. 897-98


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


4 S.W.3d 13; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 101



September 15, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPELLANT'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE FIRST COURT OF APPEALS HARRIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals of Harris County (Texas) rejecting his claim that appellee could not raise the issue of reasonable suspicion at a criminal suppression hearing because the state received an adverse ruling on that issue in an earlier license revocation hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, who had moved to suppress evidence in his prosecution for driving while intoxicated, argued that appellee was estopped from litigating whether officers had reasonable suspicion to stop his car, because the public safety department got an adverse ruling on the issue at an earlier hearing to revoke his license. Appellee argued that collateral estoppel did not apply. The court agreed with appellee. The court first noted that the public safety department and the district attorney were not the same parties for collateral estoppel purposes. The court then found that Tex. Transp. Code §§ 524.012(e)(3) and 724.048(a)(3), providing that an administrative judge's decision on an issue did not preclude litigation on the same facts in a criminal proceeding, were not unconstitutional, because the administrative proceeding was civil and double jeopardy concerns were not implicated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that double jeopardy concerns were not implicated because the license revocation proceeding was not criminal, and that as such, collateral estoppel did not apply to prevent the district attorney from litigating the reasonable suspicion issue.

Sanchez v. State


NO. 1259-98


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


995 S.W.2d 677; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 89; 80 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 267



June 30, 1999, Delivered

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversed, and the case remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of a judgment from the Fourth Court of Appeals, Bexar County (Texas) that dismissed defendant's conviction, having found that the sexual harassment provision of Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 39.03(a) was unconstitutionally vague on its face and as applied to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under the sexual harassment provision of the official oppression statute, Tex. Pen. Code § 39.03(a)(3). Defendant appealed, and the court of appeals found that the provision was unconstitutionally vague on its face and as applied to his conduct. The prosecution appealed. The court held that the sexual harassment provision was constitutional on its face and as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding the sexual harassment provision of the Texas official oppression statute unconstitutionally vague was reversed and remanded. The court held that the phrase "unwelcome sexual advances, requests for sexual favors, and other verbal or physical conduct of a sexual nature" was reasonably specific for Due Process purposes.

Ex parte Carrio


NOS. 73,180 and 73,181


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


992 S.W.2d 486; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 56



May 26, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Ex parte Carrio, 9 S.W.3d 163, 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 139 (Tex. Crim. App., 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR A WRIT OF HABEAS CORPUS FROM HARRIS COUNTY.
Carrio v. State, 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5878 (Tex. App., July 12, 1984)



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction writ of habeas corpus held in abeyance pending trial court's compliance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the District Court of Harris County (Texas) denying defendant's application for habeas corpus relief filed pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 11.07 for defendant's murder and attempted murder convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and attempted murder. Fourteen years later defendant filed an application for habeas corpus relief and alleged that he suffered ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The trial court denied defendant's application based on the doctrine of laches. Defendant appealed. The court reversed and held that delay alone was insufficient to deny defendant's application. The prosecution had the burden to make a particularized showing of prejudice, to show that defendant's late application caused the prejudice, and to show that defendant failed to act with reasonable diligence as a matter of law. After the prosecution made such a showing, defendant was required to show that the prosecution was not prejudiced or that defendant's delay in filing the application was justified. While the trial court accurately determined that defendant filed the application 14 years after the convictions, the trial court failed to resolve the remaining issues.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying defendant's application for habeas corpus relief and held that defendant's delay in filing an application for writ of habeas corpus was insufficient alone to deny defendant's application.

Fuentes v. State


NO. 72,700


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7880.

Writ of habeas corpus denied Fuentes v. Dretke, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 2296 (5th Cir. Tex., Feb. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM HARRIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 and sentenced to death, sought direct review of the Harris County Court (Texas) judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of a capital murder, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03, after he was found to have shot and killed a person in conjunction with having robbed a convenience store. Appellant was sentenced to death and therefore obtained an automatic appeal. While appellant raised several points of error, the court overruled each one and affirmed the judgment below. Among appellant's arguments was that he was denied his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to effective assistance of counsel when trial counsel failed to request a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of felony murder. The court found that there was no evidence that would have permitted a jury to rationally find that appellant had the intent to commit the robbery, but not to cause the death of the victim. Accordingly, appellant was not entitled to a charge on the lesser-included offense of felony murder. Having failed to establish that he was entitled to the instruction, the court held that appellant could not establish that his counsel's performance fell below professional standards.


OUTCOME: The judgment below convicting appellant of murder and sentencing him to death was affirmed because the court overruled each of appellant's points of error, including appellant's claim that he was denied ineffective assistance due to his counsel's failure to request an instruction on a lesser-included offense. The court found that appellant was not entitled to the instruction.

Jackson v. State


NO.72,622


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


992 S.W.2d 469; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 42



April 28, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM HARRIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) and sentenced to death, sought a direct appeal from the judgment of the Harris County (Texas) court pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(h).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2). Appeal was automatic under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(h). Appellant raised numerous points of error, but the court overruled each one and affirmed the judgment below. Among the arguments raised by appellant was that the court erred by refusing to order payment of a polygraph examiner to assist appellant's defense as an indigent. The court rejected this argument and contrasted the use of a polygraph expert in appellant's case against the use of other types of experts, such as psychiatrists, that have been shown to be necessary to the defense in some cases. Here, the court found that appellant made no showing that there was a significant issue of fact which the knowledge of a lay jury would not be expected to encompass. The issue instead was the credibility of two witnesses, appellant and a police officer, who gave different versions of a conversation between them. The court found that this was precisely the kind of issue on which courts routinely turn to lay juries for resolution and thus the use of a polygraph examiner was not required.


OUTCOME: The judgment below incorporating appellant's conviction for murder and sentence to death was affirmed because the court overruled each of appellant's points of error, including appellant's claim that, as an indigent, he was entitled to a court-appointed polygraph examiner.

 

130 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


NO. 72,638


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


999 S.W.2d 385; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 35



April 21, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied June 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3843.
Writ of certiorari denied Moore v. Texas, 530 U.S. 1216, 120 S. Ct. 2220, 147 L. Ed. 2d 252, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3843 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Application denied by Moore v. Dretke, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 4995 (W.D. Tex., Mar. 23, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Stay denied by, Injunction denied by Ex parte Moore, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1230 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM BEXAR COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from Bexar County (Texas) after he was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and was sentenced to death. Appellant was found guilty of shooting a peace officer. Appellant brought 37 points of error on appeal. The court affirmed. The court disagreed with appellant that his comments and outbursts, mental health history, and decision to represent himself during portions of the trial constituted evidence warranting a competency hearing. The court also found the record showed appellant's decision to proceed pro se was knowing, intelligent and voluntary. Thus, his decision to self-representation was not evidence of incompetency. The court also found appellant was not entitled to a new trial based on the allegation that the record on appeal omitted portions of the trial proceedings because appellant did not take steps to cure the deficiency in the record. The court did not err in failing to instruct on the lesser included offense of murder or not guilty by reason of insanity. The court found all of appellant's other points of error were also without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of capital murder and sentence to death, finding all of appellant's points of error were without merit. The court found appellant was not entitled to a new trial, and the court found the record lacked evidence that appellant should have been given a competency hearing.

132 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Busby v. State


NO. 72,539


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


990 S.W.2d 263; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 26



March 31, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied January 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIs 212.
Writ of certiorari denied Busby v. Texas, 528 U.S. 1081, 145 L. Ed. 2d 676, 120 S. Ct. 803, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 212 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Busby v. Cockrell, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 24558 (E.D. Tex., Mar. 31, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CHEROKEE COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the trial court, Cherokee County (Texas), of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(7)(A) and sentence to death.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(7)(A) and the trial judge sentenced appellant to death. Appellant challenged his conviction, contending that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion to change venue because the State failed to properly controvert his motion to change venue. In support of his motion to change venue, appellant filed two affidavits alleging he could not obtain a fair trial in the county. In response, the State filed two affidavits, which its affiants contradicted on the witness stand. The court held there was no reason to believe that supporting and controverting affidavits necessarily served the same purposes and hence no reason to believe that they must conform to the same requirements. Appellant further contended that the trial court erred in permitting the parties to exercise peremptory challenges at the end of voir dire, a procedure for non-capital cases. The court found that the procedure controlling the order and timing of the exercise of peremptory challenges was not an absolute requirement. Appellant waived any error by requesting the procedure followed in the present case. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder and sentence to death, overruling all appellants' points of error.

Brooks v. State


NO. 72,806


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


990 S.W.2d 278; 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 27



March 31, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7013.
Rehearing denied by, 05/27/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Brooks v. Texas, 528 U.S. 956, 120 S. Ct. 384, 145 L. Ed. 2d 300, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7013 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Motion dismissed by Brooks v. Dretke, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 30467 (W.D. Tex., June 2, 2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Brooks v. Dretke, 404 F.3d 924, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 4957 (5th Cir. Tex., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of conviction for capital murder and death sentence under Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(2) and Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(g), in appellee prosecution's favor, in the Bexar County Court (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged several errors on appeal of a capital murder conviction and imposition of a death sentence under Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(2), Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(g). The court first rejected appellant's argument that the evidence was legally insufficient to support the aggravating elements which elevated the offense to capital murder. The court concluded sufficient evidence of appellant's robbery and kidnapping of the victim prior to shooting him was shown. The court explained a rational trier of fact could have found appellant's kidnapping and robbery beyond a reasonable doubt. The court next found the evidence was factually sufficient because the jury could have found witness testimony credible. The court explained a factual sufficiency challenge was viewed in the light most favorable to the prosecution and a verdict was set aside only if it was so contrary to the overwhelming weight of the evidence as to be clearly unjust and wrong. The court found the jury properly considered relevant future dangerousness factors, and the evidence was legally sufficient to support its finding on future dangerousness finding. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's capital murder conviction and death sentence, in appellee prosecution's favor, because the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support aggravating elements which elevated offense to capital murder, the jury verdict, and jury findings on future dangerousness. The court found no error in the admission of a present sense impression hearsay exception and the denial of a juror challenge for cause.

 

134 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hulit v. State


NO. 877-97


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


982 S.W.2d 431; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 174



December 16, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 2ND COURT OF APPEALS. TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 2nd Court of Appeals, Tarrant County (Texas), which affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated under Tex. Penal Code §§49.04, 49.09(b). Appellant claimed that his conviction resulted from an unlawful search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: After the appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§49.04, 49.09(b), appellant sought review. On appeal, the issue was whether the search and seizure provision of the Texas constitution was violated when an officer went to the aid of a motorist who was unconscious in his vehicle on a public highway. The court affirmed the conviction, concluding that the Tex. Const. art. I § 9 contained no requirement that a seizure or search be authorized by warrant and that a seizure or search that was otherwise reasonable would not be found in violation of that section because it was not authorized by a warrant. Moreover, the court determined that there was no violation of the supremacy clause of U.S. Const. Art. VI. Finally, the court noted that appellant could have invoked the protections of U.S. Const. Amend. IV. Having requested protection only under Article I § 9, however, appellant forfeited any protections he was entitled to under U.S. Const. Amend. IV. The protections were available; appellant simply chose not to avail himself of them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because under the Texas Constitution, there was no requirement that a seizure or search be authorized by warrant, and a seizure or search that was otherwise reasonable was permissible even if not authorized by a warrant.

Ex parte Bates


NOS. 73,099 and 73,100


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


978 S.W.2d 575; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 135



October 21, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Habeas Corpus Application from PARKER County.



DISPOSITION: Relief granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Texas), which sentenced him to 18 months confinement on each of two counts of delivery of less than five pounds of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner applicant was convicted of two counts of delivery of less than five pounds of marijuana and placed on probation for five years. Thereafter, the court revoked his probation, and he was sentenced to 18 months confinement in a state jail felony facility in each cause. On appeal, petitioner contended that he had not received credit for all the time he was confined in these causes before being sentenced. Petitioner was confined for several months before he pled guilty and was placed on community supervision, and was again confined for several months, pending respondent state's motion to revoke his community supervision. Reversing the trial court judgment in part, the court held that credit must be granted for periods of confinement pursuant to motions to revoke community supervision. The court further held that denying credit for such periods of confinement would violate due course of law under Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19, by deterring persons from exercising their constitutional right to a revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in part, by granting petitioner applicant credit for the period of confinement pursuant to the motion to revoke community supervision because to hold otherwise might encourage defendants to waive their constitutional right to a revocation hearing.

Satterwhite v. State


NO. 1474-97


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


979 S.W.2d 626; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 114



September 23, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition For Discretionary Review from the Thirteenth Court of Appeals (Jackson County).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the determination by the 13th Court of Appeals (Texas) affirming his conviction under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.122 for practicing without a license despite appellant's payment of past due bar dues.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney was convicted of falsely holding himself out as a lawyer under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.122, and the appellate court affirmed. Appellant had represented a defendant as attorney of record during a time his license was suspended for nonpayment of bar dues. Appellant paid past-due state bar dues and argued that, as a result, the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain his conviction. On discretionary review, the court affirmed the appellate court's decision, holding that the retroactive return to active status did not excuse appellant from prosecution. The court reasoned that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. title 2 app. G (1996) (Tex. State Bar R. art. X, § 9) did not effect prosecution under § 38.122, but only effected the ability of appellant to become reinstated without being readmitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court which affirmed the conviction of appellant attorney because he had represented a client while suspended and payment of past due bar dues and reinstatement did not effect his prosecution for practicing without a license.

Mosley v. State


NO. 72,281


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


983 S.W.2d 249; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 86



July 1, 1998, Delivered


NOTICE:   [**1] PUBLISH IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2656.
Rehearing denied by, 09/16/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Mosley v. Texas, 526 U.S. 1070, 119 S. Ct. 1466, 143 L. Ed. 2d 550, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2656 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Stay denied by Ex parte Mosley, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 450 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from GREGG County.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of May 20, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 67.
Mosley v. State, 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 67 (Tex. Crim. App., 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant automatically appealed the order of the trial court (Texas) that convicted him of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(2) and imposed the death penalty upon him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(2), and he was sentenced to death. His appeal was automatic. The court held that there was sufficient evidence that defendant shot and killed the victims during the course of a planned robbery, that selection of the grand jury foreman did not violate equal protection, that the judge's relationship to an investigating police officer was harmless, that federal peace officers may question a defendant, and that the exclusion of an additional witness's testimony was harmless. The court also concluded that closing remarks directed at defendant's counsel did not cause defendant prejudice. During the penalty phase, the trial court had admitted victim impact testimony, which included victim character evidence; however, defendant did not waive the mitigation issue for the penalty phase. The court held that although some character evidence was admitted, it was intertwined with the impact of the victim's loss on family members, and it served the function of humanizing the victims. Finally, the court rejected 64 points of error as being inadequately briefed and affirmed the conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's capital murder conviction and the death penalty imposed upon him for that crime because there was sufficient evidence to establish that defendant shot and killed four victims during a planned robbery. Moreover, the trial court properly admitted evidence of victims' character during penalty phase because the evidence was intertwined with impact evidence, and defendant did not waive mitigation issue.

Johnson v. State


NO. 1399-96


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


967 S.W.2d 848; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 39



March 25, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition For Discretionary Review from the Second Court of Appeals. (Tarrant County).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for discretionary review from the Second Court of Appeals of Tarrant County (Texas) seeking review of the judgment affirming a conviction for indecency with a child. Defendant sought to determine whether the offense required a culpable mental state relating to the child's age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of the offense of indecency with a child, and the jury assessed punishment at confinement for two years, probated for a period of five years. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant filed a petition for discretionary review to determine whether the offense of indecency with a child required a culpable mental state relating to the child's age. The court granted the petition and affirmed the judgment. The court held that in cases involving the sexual assault of a child, such as rape of a child or indecency with a child, the state was not required to show that a defendant knew the victim to be younger than 17 years of age. The court concluded that requiring the state to allege and prove defendant knew the victim to have been under the age of 17 would establish ignorance or mistake as a defense in contravention of the clear legislative intent of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11.


OUTCOME: The judgment upholding defendant's conviction was affirmed. In cases involving the sexual assault of a child, the state was not required to show that a defendant knew the victim was younger than 17 years of age. Requiring the state to do so would establish ignorance or mistake as a defense in contravention of clear legislative intent.

Raby v. State


NO. 71,938


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


970 S.W.2d 1; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 27



March 4, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 16, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 7313.
Rehearing denied by, 04/22/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Raby v. Texas, 525 U.S. 1003, 119 S. Ct. 515, 142 L. Ed. 2d 427, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 7313 (Nov. 16, 1998)
Post-conviction proceeding at Raby v. Dretke, 78 Fed. Appx. 324, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 20943 (5th Cir. Tex., Oct. 15, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Raby v. State, 2015 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 323 (Tex. Crim. App., Apr. 22, 2015)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Ex parte Raby, 2017 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 387 (Tex. Crim. App., May 17, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from HARRIS County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Harris County Court (Texas), which convicted him for capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: In his challenge to his capital murder conviction and death sentence, appellant claimed he was erroneously denied the right to voir dire prospective jurors on whether they could consider particular types of mitigation, such as voluntary intoxication. He also contended that the trial court erred in denying him an evidentiary hearing on his claim that the death penalty was administered in a racially discriminatory manner. The court concluded that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.04(b), which permitted a voluntary intoxication defense only if it rose to the level of temporary insanity, was constitutional. Further, appellant was not entitled to an instruction on what evidence was mitigating or on what weight the jury was to give any mitigating evidence presented at trial. Appellant failed to supply evidence showing that racial considerations play a part in imposition of the death sentence in his case. He also failed to show that it was cruel or unusual punishment. The court found no improprieties in the trial court's procedures or application of the laws warranting reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed imposition of the death sentence upon appellant's conviction for capital murder. Appellant failed to show violation or his constitutional rights, improper application of the statute under which charged, or improper jury instructions and proceedings.

State v. Terrazas


NO. 1628-96


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


962 S.W.2d 38; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 16



February 4, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review from the Eighth Court of Appeals. EL PASO County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee below sought discretionary review from the Eighth Court of Appeals, El Paso County (Texas), which reversed the trial court order dismissing the indictment against appellee, and suppressed appellee's statement. The lower appellate court reversed, holding that the trial court lacked authority to dismiss the indictment with prejudice and that the trial court abused its discretion in granting the motion to suppress the statement.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was indicted for tampering with a governmental record, by allegedly making a false entry in an application for assistant from the Texas Department of Human Services (DHS). Appellee filed a pretrial motion to dismiss the indictment and to suppress her statement. Appellee contended that her rights to due process and due course of law under the United States Constitution and the Texas Constitution were violated because the county attorney's office was compensated by DHS for accepting cases submitted by it for prosecution. The trial court dismissed, and the state sought review. The lower appellate court reversed, holding that a trial court could not dismiss an indictment with prejudice without the prosecutor's consent, except as authorized by the constitution, a statute, or common law. Appellee sought discretionary review. The court reversed and remanded, holding that under certain circumstances a trial court did have authority to dismiss, and on remand the lower appellate court should determine whether dismissal by the trial court was required to remove the taint of any constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower appellate court which entered an order reversing the trial court order dismissing the indictment against appellee, and suppressing appellee's statement. The court held that under certain circumstances, not considered by the appellate court, the trial court had authority to dismiss a charging instrument. The court remanded for determination of whether the trial court properly dismissed the indictment.

McGinn v. State


NO. 72,134


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


961 S.W.2d 161; 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



January 21, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from BROWN County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the trial court (Texas), which convicted him of capital murder. The jury answered the punishment issues in the State's favor, and appellant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murdering a 12-year-old girl and sentenced to death by a jury. Prior to trial there had been a great deal of publicity surrounding the murder. Newspaper articles referred to a murder charge of which appellant was acquitted and referred to fairly recent murders of two other girls in the county. The court affirmed finding the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a request for change of venue because the record did not establish appellant's inability to obtain a fair trial. The court held that because appellant did not request an inquiry into a child's competence to testify, he could not complain about the trial court's failure to do so. The court held it was not error for the trial court to refuse to instruct on the minimum eligibility requirements for parole in a capital case nor in instructing the jury not to consider any possible action by the parole board. The court held it did not conduct sufficiency review of the mitigation special issue. The court found that a factual sufficiency review of a jury's determination of a probability of future dangerousness was not required by the Texas Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to change venue because of prejudicial pretrial publicity. Appellant's failure to request an inquiry into a child's competence to testify waived the issue. The trial court did not err in refusing to instruct on the minimum eligibility requirements for parole in a capital case nor in instructing the jury not to consider any possible action by the parole board.

 

146 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Tennard


NO. 71,678


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


960 S.W.2d 57; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 109



December 18, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied June 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4343.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas Corpus Application From Harris County.



DISPOSITION: All requested relief is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applicant brought a petition for writ of habeas corpus seeking relief from the judgment of the District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of capital murder and sentenced him to death based upon the special issues presented to the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071(b)(1) and (2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant applicant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant sought habeas corpus relief claiming that the special issues required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071(b)(1) and (2) did not allow the jury to give mitigating effect to evidence in violation of U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV. The court held that the special issues allowed the jury to give mitigating effect to evidence of defendant's youth and his youthful incarceration. The court held that there was no "nexus" between defendant's youthful incarceration and circumstances of the offense that tended to excuse the commission of the offense. The court held that evidence of defendant's low IQ did not, standing alone, establish mental retardation. The court held that there was no evidence that defendant's low IQ rendered him unable to appreciate the wrongfulness of his conduct or diminished his ability to control his impulses or evaluate the consequences of his conduct. The court held that the jury could have given mitigating effect to his low IQ and that there was no danger that the jury would have given any mitigating qualities of such evidence only aggravating effect.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant applicant's petition for habeas corpus seeking relief from his conviction of capital murder and sentence of death because the special issues submitted to the jury allowed the jury to give mitigating effect to evidence of defendant's youth, his youthful incarceration, and his low IQ. The court held that evidence of defendant's low IQ was insufficient, by itself, to establish mental retardation.

 

147 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Henderson v. State


No. 72,157


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


962 S.W.2d 544; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 104



December 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 7104.
Rehearing denied by, 03/04/1998
Concurring Opinion at, Dissenting Opinion at Henderson v. State, 977 S.W.2d 605, 1998 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 84 (Tex. Crim. App., 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied, Motion denied by Henderson v. Texas, 525 U.S. 978, 119 S. Ct. 437, 142 L. Ed. 2d 356, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 7104 (1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Henderson v. Dretke, 164 Fed. Appx. 506, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 2190 (5th Cir. Tex., 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ex parte Henderson, 246 S.W.3d 690, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 769 (Tex. Crim. App., 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by Ex parte Henderson, 2012 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1605 (Tex. Crim. App., Dec. 5, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of a trial court in Travis County (Texas), which convicted her of capital murder of an infant under her care in violation of Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(8), and sentenced her to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of her conviction of capital murder of an infant under her care under Tex. Penal Code § 19.03(a)(8). The court held that maps drawn by appellant were privileged, but that the attorney-client privilege was required to yield to the strong public policy interest of protecting a child from death or serious bodily injury. The court held that defendant's right against self-incrimination was not violated by counsel's disclosure of privileged information because there was evidence that no disclosure was made and counsel was not an agent of the government. The court held that § 19.03(a)(8) did not violate equal protection because the state had a compelling interest in protecting children and the statute was rationally related to serve this interest. The court held that § 19.03(a)(8) did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII because it only applied to a subclass of convicted murderers and the "children under six" category was clear and definite. Appellant's confession was voluntary and not induced by any positive promise. Testimony that appellant admitted that she committed a murder was highly probative of guilt and was offered as an admission of the primary offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's capital murder conviction because privileged evidence concerning infant's location was properly disclosed where attorney-client privilege was required to yield to strong public policy in protecting child from death. The statute under which appellant was convicted was constitutional. Appellant's confession was voluntary because it was not obtained by any promise and it was supported by sufficient evidence.

Tuttle v. State


No. 72,387


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 87



November 5, 1997, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from SMITH County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted murder challenged the judgment of the trial court (Texas), which convicted him of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2). Appellant also sought review of his sentence to death pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.071(2)(g).


OVERVIEW: Appellant convicted murderer killed his friend's aunt in order to steal her car and her credit cards. After the murder, he took the victim's car and used her credit cards. Appellant was arrested and convicted of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) and later sentenced to death pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.071(2)(g). On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction and his sentence. The court held that the evidence was both legally and factually sufficient to support the jury's finding that there was a probability that appellant would commit criminal acts of violence that would constitute a continuing threat to society. The court further held that appellant's confession was admissible because the police's conduct did not rise to level of coercive conduct so as to render appellant's statement involuntary. Moreover, the court held that appellant did not invoke his U.S. Const. amend V right to an attorney when he was being interrogated and therefore his confession was admissible. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not err by allowing victim impact evidence at the punishment phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction, holding the evidence was both legally and factually sufficient to support the jury's finding that there was a probability that appellant would commit criminal acts of violence that would constitute a continuing threat to society. The court held that given the sufficient of the evidence, appellant convicted murderer's sentence to death was appropriate.

 

149 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


NO. 72,244


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


958 S.W.2d 186; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 79



October 15, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from MONTGOMERY County.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated and cause remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision Montgomery County trial court (Texas) that convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of capital murder and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant argued, among other things, that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a trial court decision that convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of capital murder and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant contended, among other things, that there was insufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction and death sentence. The court affirmed defendant's conviction but reversed the imposed death sentence and remanded for resentencing. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. Defendant's extrajudicial confession that he killed his victim for her rings was properly admitted because the confession was supported by corroborating evidence, including that the murder scene itself showed signs of robbery. There was sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding that defendant was a continuing danger to society. The trial court error in denying defendant's motion for leave to file for expert assistance ex parte. The prosecution failed to prove that the disclosure that defendant's motion was for a mental health expert did not contribute to the jury's verdict at punishment. The admission of victim and crime scene photographs was proper because such photographs were relevant and not unduly prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's capital murder conviction but reversed defendant's death sentence and remanded for resentencing. There was sufficient evidence, including defendant's corroborated extrajudicial confession and defendant posing continuing threat to society, to support defendant's conviction. By requiring defendant to disclose his expert mental health witness request, it could not be said that such did not contribute to the verdict.

King v. State


NO. 72,145


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


953 S.W.2d 266; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 71



September 24, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the trial court, Jefferson County (Texas), which convicted defendant of capital murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence on appeal, but he claimed that the trial court made errors in the jury selection and improperly admitted hearsay evidence. He also asserted that the death penalty was unconstitutional and arbitrarily enforced. The court rejected defendant's claims. The court found that defendant did not object to the manner in which the trial court provided notice that the venire panel had been exhausted. Defendant's claim that certain jurors should have been excluded where they had a bias or prejudice against the minimum sentence for murder was rejected because the lesser included offense of murder did not contribute to defendant's conviction or punishment. The court also ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting excited utterances of a witness, a hotel registration card bearing defendant's name, or packets containing information regarding defendant's previous incarcerations in the Texas Department of Criminal Justice. The court further held that the death penalty sentence was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder and death sentence.

 

151 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ibarra


No. 1360-95


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


953 S.W.2d 242; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 58



September 10, 1997, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review from the Fourteenth Court of Appeals [Chambers County].



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the suppression by the 14th Court of Appeals, Chambers County (Texas) of evidence against appellee on the grounds that the state failed to prove voluntariness of consent by clear and convincing evidence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress evidence seized during the search of his car on the ground that he did not voluntarily consent to the search. The trial court found the state proved voluntariness by a preponderance of the evidence but not by clear and convincing evidence as required under Tex. Const. art. I, § 9. On appeal, the state sought to lower the burden of proof, contending that the Tex. Constitution demanded only that it prove voluntariness of consent by a preponderance of the evidence. The court affirmed, holding, as it consistently had, that the state must prove the voluntariness of a consent to search by clear and convincing evidence. The state failed to offer any compelling reason to change the standard of proof, and changing it would undermine years of well-established precedent.


OUTCOME: The suppression of evidence was affirmed because the state failed to prove voluntariness of consent to search by clear and convincing evidence.

 

152 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fritz v. State


NO. 1429-95


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


946 S.W.2d 844; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 48



June 11, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 13, 1997. Second Correction October 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Discretionary Review from the FOURTH Court of Appeals. BEXAR County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Fourth Court of Appeals, Bexar County (Texas), which affirmed his conviction of capital murder and held that state's use of peremptory challenges on seven male veniremembers did not constitute gender discrimination in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: During jury selection, appellant objected to state's peremptory challenges of seven male veniremembers alleging gender discrimination. State responded that it removed all males under the age of 30 because of their potential bias or shared identity with appellant. Appellant's objection was overruled, and he was convicted of capital murder. The court of appeals affirmed the conviction, holding that the trial court's findings on the gender discrimination issue were not clearly erroneous. The court held that the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV prohibited discrimination in jury selection on the basis of gender, or on the assumption that an individual would be biased in a particular case for no reason other than the fact that the person happened to be a woman or happened to be a man. The court held that state's explanation that the male veniremembers might have possessed a "potential bias" or "common ground" with appellant was not a neutral explanation. The court reversed the conviction, holding that the male veniremembers were excluded on the basis of gender in violation of the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, which had affirmed appellant's capital murder conviction, and remanded the case to the trial court. State's peremptory challenges of male veniremembers based on "potential bias" or "common ground" with appellant unconstitutionally excluded from the jury veniremembers on the basis of gender.

 

153 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Green v. State


NO. 1380-95


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


951 S.W.2d 3; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 41



June 4, 1997, DELIVERED


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review from the Second court of Appeals [DENTON County].



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment from the Second Court of Appeals, Denton County (Texas), which held that the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to quash the information because the information failed to allege that defendant knew the requesting person was a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the trial court's decision to deny his motion to quash the state's information for failure to allege that defendant knew the requesting person was a peace officer. The appellate court reversed, holding that the trial court erred in failing to grant defendant's motion, and the state sought review. The court affirmed, holding that a misdemeanor information charging an offense under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.02 must contain an allegation that the accused knew the person requesting information was a peace officer. The state contended that the language employed in the statute, when construed in light of other statutes in Tex. Penal Code Ann § 38, necessarily included the concept of knowledge regarding the requesting individual's status, and that because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.02(b)(2) used the language "lawfully detained," it inherently included the knowledge requirement. The court held that in a prosecution under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.02, the state must allege that the person who refused to give identification or gave false identification knew the individual requesting the identification was a peace officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment in favor of defendant, and holding that the trial court erred in failing to grant defendant's motion to quash in an action claiming failure to identify. The court held that the state must allege that the person who refused to give identification or gave false identification knew the individual requesting the identification was a peace officer.

Johnson v. State


NO. 72,046


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 28



April 30, 1997, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Johnson v. Texas, 528 U.S. 835, 120 S. Ct. 95, 145 L. Ed. 2d 81, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5258 (1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ex parte Johnson, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1293 (Tex. Crim. App., July 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from HARRIS County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the verdict from the trial court in Harris County (Texas), that convicted him of capital murder in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a) and sentenced appellant to death pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.0711, § 3(g), and admitted victim impact evidence over appellant's objection.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder. During the punishment phase the trial court admitted, over appellant's objection, victim impact evidence. The jury was required to answer a special issue that asked about appellant's personal moral culpability. The jury's instructions included language about evidence affecting appellant's moral blameworthiness. Appellant was sentenced to death and review to the Texas supreme court was automatic under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.0711, § 3(j). The court applied a seven-part test to determine the admissibility of the victim impact evidence. The court found that appellant's general objection to all victim impact evidence was not specific enough to preserve error on appeal. Rather, a specific objection had to be made to each objectionable statement or group of statements. Appellant did not object during the testimony nor did he cross-examine the witnesses. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence because the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it admitted victim impact evidence over appellant's general objection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence because appellant failed to specifically object to each objectionable victim impact statement, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it admitted the victim impact evidence over appellant's general objection.

Lagrone v. State


No. 71,731


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


942 S.W.2d 602; 1997 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 10



February 5, 1997, DELIVERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 7, 1997. Second Correction February 13, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 14, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6094.
Corrected by, 02/07/1997
Corrected by, 02/13/1997
Rehearing denied by, 04/09/1997
Writ of certiorari denied LaGrone v. Texas, 522 U.S. 917, 139 L. Ed. 2d 235, 118 S. Ct. 305, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6094 (1997)
Magistrate's recommendation at Lagrone v. Johnson, 2000 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 21738 (N.D. Tex., Nov. 2, 2000)
Motion dismissed by Ex parte Lagrone, 2004 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 201 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's death sentence was automatically appealed under Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. Art. 37.071 (h) from the Criminal District Court of Tarrant County (Texas). Defendant was convicted of capital murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(6)(A). At the punishment phase, the jury answered the issues of Tex. Crim. Proc. Code art. 37.071 (b)(1) and (2) affirmatively.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of capital murder for the murder of more than one person in the same criminal transaction pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(6)(A) (1993). Defendant was sentenced to death after the jury answered the special issues related to aggravating and mitigating circumstances. Defendant objected to issues relating to limitations on jury voir dire, being examined by a state-sponsored psychiatrist regarding future dangerousness, and excluding evidence of a witness's drug addiction. The court held that the trial court could limit jury voir dire regarding the meaning of the word probability, and the meaning of probability was not constitutionally vague. The trial court could order defendant to submit to an independent state-sponsored psychiatric exam prior to the presentation of defendant's expert testimony when defendant demonstrated his intent to put on future dangerousness expert testimony. The trial court properly excluded cross-examination regarding a witness's drug addiction when defendant did not show that the witness's perceptual capacity was physically impaired. All other issues that defendant raised were also overruled and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant was properly sentenced to death because the issues he raised relating to jury voir dire, being examined by a state-sponsored psychiatrist about future dangerousness; and excluding evidence of a witness's drug addiction were overruled .
