Sonnier v. State


NO. 71,698


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


913 S.W.2d 511; 1995 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 123



November 29, 1995, DELIVERED  
November 29, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, 01/10/1996
Habeas corpus proceeding at Sonnier v. Quarterman, 476 F.3d 349, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 1336 (5th Cir. Tex., 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by Sonnier, 2008 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 414 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Harris County. 179th District Court of Harris County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the 179th District Court of Harris County (Texas), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of capital murder and sentencing him to death, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2, upon evidence that defendant had stabbed a woman and bludgeoned her to death with a hammer and had fatally stabbed the woman's infant child.


OVERVIEW: A woman and her infant child were found dead in their home. The child had been stabbed, while the woman had been stabbed, strangled, and beaten with a hammer. Defendant was seen walking nearby with a bloody towel and his abandoned clothes were later found with blood on them, together with a bloody cord. Blood and DNA testing were mostly inconclusive, except that one of his socks contained blood matching the dead woman's blood. Defendant was charged with and convicted of capital murder. The jury found he was a continuing threat to society, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that, although entirely circumstantial, there was sufficient evidence to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant committed the murders and to support the finding that he remained a continuing threat, given the needless and vicious brutality of the murders. Also, crime scene photographs and videotape were admissible to show the reality of the brutal crime. The sentencing scheme of Article 37.071 did not violate due process or equal protection and did not permit cruel and unusual punishments.


OUTCOME: The conviction and death sentence were affirmed because, inter alia, they were supported by sufficient evidence that defendant was the perpetrator of the double murder and that he remained a continuing threat to society due to the extreme brutality and vicious nature of the crimes; the death penalty statute was not unconstitutional; and it was not improper to admit into evidence crime scene photographs and videotape.

 

199 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Curry v. State


No. 71,630


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


910 S.W.2d 490; 1995 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 119



November 22, 1995, Delivered  
November 22, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Certificate of appealability denied Curry v. Johnson, 228 F.3d 408, 2000 U.S. App. LEXIS 18816 (5th Cir. Tex., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from TRAVIS County. 167th District Court of Travis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for capital murder entered in the 167th District Court of Travis County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder after shooting a convenience store clerk during a robbery. Appellant sought review of his conviction, and the court affirmed. Appellant alleged several errors on appeal. One error asserted was that the trial court erred in overruling appellant's challenge for cause to one venire member who had expressed an opinion as to appellant's guilt. In order for a challenge for cause to be sustained under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 35.16(a)(10), appellant had to show that the venire member had established in his mind a conclusion as to his guilt or innocence and that this conclusion would influence his verdict. Though the venire member here had expressed an opinion as to appellant's guilt, there was no indication that his opinion would affect his decision during deliberations. Another error alleged was the failure of the trial court to grant a mistrial based upon the state's failure to disclose that a third person had confessed to the murder. The state only had to disclose material evidence, which was evidence that had a reasonable probability of effecting the outcome. The trial court found no probability here because the statement was recanted.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for capital murder was affirmed. The trial court did not err in overruling appellant's challenge for cause to a venire member who had expressed an opinion as to appellant's guilt because there was no indication that the venireperson's opinion would affect his deliberations. No mistrial was warranted on the basis of the state's failure to disclose a recanted confession by a third person.

 

200 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ieppert v. State


NO. 826-92, 827-92, 829-92, 830-92


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


908 S.W.2d 217; 1995 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 100



October 11, 1995, DELIVERED  
October 11, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review from the Fifth Court of Appeals. 363rd District Court. DALLAS COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a ruling from the Fifth Court of Appeals, 363rd District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which affirmed his convictions for aggravated sexual assault. The indictment charged a version of the offense that was not in effect at the time of the alleged crime, but appellant had not raised his objection of ex post facto violation under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 16, at the trial court level.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault in four cases consolidated for prosecution. On appeal, he claimed that these convictions were barred by the ex post facto clauses of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 16 because the statute under which he was prosecuted, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021, had not yet been enacted at the time of his allegedly criminal conduct. At the first level of appellate review, the lower court did not reach the merits of this claim, however, holding instead that appellant forfeited the right to complain of it on appeal because he did not first raise it in the trial court. On further discretionary review, the court agreed with appellant and held that prosecution for conduct which was not illegal when committed was not a forfeitable irregularity of the trial process. Consequently, the court reversed the convictions and remanded for reconsideration based on the ex post facto prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's convictions for aggravated sexual assault, finding that the indictment charged an offense that was not in existence at the time of the alleged criminal conduct, and that this ex post facto violation was not waived by appellant even though he did not object at trial.
